 
 This Prospectus is a non-official and non-binding translation into English of the original “Folleto Informativo” drafted 
in Spanish language and registered with the “Comisión Nacional del Mercado de Valores” (the Spanish Securities 
Market Commission, “CNMV”) on June 7, 2005. The “Folleto Informativo” drafted in Spanish language is the only 
official document.

Issue Amount and Number of Notes: seven hundred million (700,000,000) euros comprised of seven thousand (7,000) 
Notes divided in five (5) Classes: 
 
Class A1: comprised of 1,540 Notes and with a total nominal amount of 154,000,000 euros. 
 
Class A2: comprised of 5,240 Notes and with a total nominal amount of 524,000,000 euros. 
Class B: comprised of 70 Notes and with a total nominal amount of 7,000,000 euros. 
Class C: comprised of 77 Notes and with a total nominal amount of 7,700,000 euros. 
Class D: comprised of 73 Notes and with a total nominal amount of 7,300,000 euros. 
 
¾ 
Nominal Amount: one hundred thousand (100,000) euros per Note. 
¾ 
Price of issue: one hundred thousand (100,000) euros per Note free of subscription expenses for the 
subscriber. 
¾ 
Reimbursement price: one hundred thousand (100,000) euros per Note. 
¾ 
Quarterly floating interes  rate: The interpolation between 4 Month and 5 Month Euribor for the first Interest 
Accrual Period and 3 Month Euribor for the subsequent Interest Accrual Periods, plus the following spreads 
for each Class of Notes:  
t
r
Class A1: spread ranging between 0.02% and 0.10%, both inclusive. 
Class A2: spread ranging between 0.10% and 0.20%, both inclusive. 
Class B: spread ranging between 0.16% and 0.36%, both inclusive. 
Class C: spread ranging between 0. 30% and 0.70%, both inclusive. 
Class D: spread ranging between 1.25% and 2.25%. both inclusive. 
The spread applicable to each Class of Notes, expressed as a percentage, shall be determined by the Managing 
Company, with, to the extent possible, the prior agreement of the Entidad Directora and the Underwriting Entities, 
before 11:00 hours (CET) of the day of commencement of the Subscription Period. 
The final spreads applicable to each Class of Notes shall be notified in written form by the Managing Company, before 
the commencement of the Subscription Period, to the Entidad Directo a and the Underwriting Entities, for notification to 
 
 
10 


 
potential investors which may be interested in subscribing the Notes. The Managing Company shall also notify the 
CNMV as additional information to this Prospectus. 
In the event that an agreement is not reached with the Entidad Directora and the Underwriting Entities, the Managing 
Company will determine the following final spreads on its own: 
Class A1: spread of 0.05%. 
Class A2: spread of 0.15%. 
Class B: spread of 0.26%. 
Class C: spread of 0. 50%. 
Class D: spread of 1.75%. 
¾

every year or, as the case may be, the following Business Day, the first Payment Date being October 17, 
2005.

Composition of the portfolio: mortgage loans granted to individuals for the construction, acquisition or renovation of 
residential properties or subrogations to individuals of financings to promoters for dwellings for sale or lease, fulfilling all 
requirements of Law 2/1981, of March 25, on the Mortgage Market and implementing regulations. 
Issuer: All the Mortgage Shares will be issued by Barclays Bank, S.A. (hereinafter, the “Issuer”).

Estimated nature of certain information: all the information contained in this Prospectus with regard to the hypotheses 
assumed to explain the payment of interest, repayment of principal, liquidity of the Fund, average maturity and returns 
and charts of financial flows are merely indicative, intended to better explain the financial structure of the issue, and are 
for guidance purposes only. 
Delays in payment and early repayment of the Mortgage Shares: the risk of delays in payment, default and early 
repayment of the Participated Mortgage Loans and, consequently, of the Mortgage Shares, will be borne by the 
Noteholders. The Noteholders shall have no action against the Debtors of the Participated Mortgage Loans. 
Investment in the Notes  In the event that there are significant levels of default on the Participated Mortgage Loans, 
the limited protection of the Notes may be reduced. There is no assurance that the Notes will be traded on the market 
with a minimum frequency or volume.

Payment Priority Order: The Available Funds, regardless of the date of their accrual, will be used to comply with the 
payment or withholding obligations on each Payment Date as follows: 
1st 
Payment of the taxes and/or withholdings borne by the Fund, the ordinary expenses of the Fund, including 
the management fee of the Managing Company, the fee of Barclays Bank, S.A. as Financial Agent (which may 
be higher, with the limit established in paragraph V.4.3, in the event that Barclays Bank, S.A. is replaced as 
Financial Agent and the new financial agent is not a company within Barclays Group) and the remaining 
expenses and servicing fees provided for in paragraph III.4.3, except for the fee for management of the 
Participated Mortgage Loans referred to in item 19th below. 
2nd  
Payment of extraordinary expenses of the Fund provided for in paragraph III.4.3. 
3rd  
Payment of amounts resulting from each settlement of the Interest Swap Agreement, except for the Payment 
Amount in the event of termination by reason of breach by, or subsequent external events affecting Barclays 
Bank PLC, Spanish Branch. 
4th  
Payment of accrued interest on the Class A1 and A2 Notes. 
5th  
Payment of accrued interest on the Class B Notes. In the event that on any given Payment Date the Principal 
Deficiency exceeds 150% of the Unpaid Principal Balance of the Class B, C and D Notes on such Payment 
Date, then the payment of accrued interest of the Class B Notes will be in 7th place in the payment priority 
order, after the payment of the Principal Due for Repayment of the Class A1 Notes and payment of Principal 
Due for Repayment of the Class A2 Notes which, in turn, will be in 5th and 6th place in the payment priority 
order, respectively. Such deferral of payment of interest on Class B Notes will be irreversible. Accordingly,  
upon occurrence of the same on a Payment Date, interest on Class B Notes will be deferred on each 
 
 
12 


 
subsequent Payment Date until full repayment of Class B Notes, even if the aforementioned ratio falls below 
150%. 
6th  
Payment of accrued interest on the Class C Notes. In the event that on any given Payment Date the Principal 
Deficiency exceeds 150% of the Unpaid Principal Balance of the Class C and D Notes on such Payment Date, 
then the payment of accrued interest of the Class C Notes will be in 9th place in the payment priority order, 
after the payment of the Principal Due for Repayment of the Class B Notes which, in turn, will be in 8th place 
in the payment priority order, and the order of the preceding items would be, if appropriate, subsequently 
altered as provided herein. Such deferral of payment of interest on Class C Notes will be irreversible. 
Accordingly, upon occurrence of the same on a Payment Date, interest on Class C Notes will be deferred on 
each subsequent Payment Date until full repayment of Class C Notes, even if the aforementioned ratio falls 
below 150%. 
7th  
Payment of accrued interest on the Class D Notes. In the event that on any given Payment Date the Principal 
Deficiency exceeds 200% of the Unpaid Principal Balance of the Class D Notes on such Payment Date, then 
the payment of accrued interest of the Class D Notes will be in 11th place in the payment priority order, after 
the payment of the Principal Due for Repayment of the Class C Notes which, in turn, will be in 10th place in 
the payment priority order, and the order of the preceding items would be, if appropriate, subsequently 
altered as provided herein. Such deferral of payment of interest on Class D Notes will be irreversible. 
Accordingly, upon occurrence of the same on a Payment Date, interest on Class D Notes will be deferred on 
each subsequent Payment Date until full repayment of Class D Notes, even if the aforementioned ratio falls 
below 200%. 
8th  
Payment of the Principal Due for Repayment of the Class A1 Notes in accordance with the rules for the 
“Allocation of the Available Principal Funds for Repayment between the Notes of each of the Classes” that are 
described below in this section.  
9th  
Payment of the Principal Due for Repayment of the Class A2 Notes in accordance with the rules for the 
“Allocation of the Available Principal Funds for Repayment between the Notes of each of the Classes” that are 
described below in this section.  
10th  
Payment of the Principal Due for Repayment of the Class B Notes in accordance with the rules for the 
“Allocation of the Available Principal Funds for Repayment between the Notes of each of the Classes” that are 
described below in this section. 
11th  
Payment of the Principal Due for Repayment of the Class C Notes in accordance with the rules for the 
“Allocation of the Available Principal Funds for Repayment between the Notes of each of the Classes” that are 
described below in this section. 
12th  
Payment of the Principal Due for Repayment of the Class D Notes in accordance with the rules for the 
“Allocation of the Available Principal Funds for Repayment between the Notes of each of the Classes” that are 
described below in this section. 
13th  
Withholding of an amount sufficient to replenish the Reserve Fund to its Required Amount. 
 
 
13 


 
14th 
Payment, in the event of early termination of the Swap Agreement by reason of the lack of fulfilment by, or 
subsequent external events affecting Barclays Bank PLC, Spanish Branch, of the Payment Amount which may 
result in favour of Barclays Bank PLC, Spanish Branch. 
15th

16th

Management Agreement. 
20th  
Payment of the Financial Intermediation Margin. 
Allocation of the Available Principal Funds for Repayment between the Notes of each of the Classes: 
Available Principal Funds for Repayment will be allocated for repayment of principal of all Classes in accordance with the 
following rules: 
1st Available Principal Funds for Repayment shall be fully allocated for repayment of Class A1 Notes until the Payment 
Date on which Class A1 Notes have been fully repaid. 
2nd Once Class A1 Notes have been fully repaid and until the first Payment Date (included) on which the Unpaid 
Principal Balance of Class B, Class C and Class D Notes represents at least 6.3% of the Unpaid Principal Balance of all 
Classes of Notes, the Available Principal Funds for Repayment shall be solely allocated for repayment of Class A2 Notes.  
3rd After the Payment Date on which the ratio between the Unpaid Principal Balance of Class B, Class C and Class D 
Notes and the Unpaid Principal Balance of all Classes of Notes, is equal or greater than 6.3%, the Available Principal 
Funds for Repayment shall be allocated for repayment of Class A2, B, C and D Notes, pro rata among them, in such a 
way that the ratio remains at 6.3% or the nearest higher percentage. 
This notwithstanding, pro rata repayment of Class A2, B, C and D Notes shall be interrupted and the Available Principal 
Funds for Repayment shall be allocated for repayment of the Classes on a sequential basis in accordance with their 
priority order on any Payment Date on which any of the following circumstances occurs: 
a) 
The Principal Balance of the Mortgage Shares with a delay in payment of overdue amounts greater than 
ninety (90) days is higher than 2% of the Principal Balance of the Mortgage Shares on the Calculation Date 
corresponding to the current Payment Date. 
b) 
The amount of the Reserve Fund is lower than its Required Amount. 
Once the circumstances producing the interruption in the pro rata repayment of Classes A2, B, C and D have 
disappeared, the referred pro rata repayment will be carried out again.  
 
 
14 


 
4th After the first Payment Date on which the amount of the Mortgage Shares pending repayment is lower than 10% of 
their initial amount, pro rata repayment of Classes A2, B, C and D Notes shall be interrupted and the Available Principal 
Funds for Repayment shall be allocated for repayment of the Classes on a sequential basis in accordance with their 
priority order until their repayment is completed. 
Exceptional rules of priority for payments made f om the Fund:  
r
In the event Barclays Bank, S.A. is replaced as Manager of the Participated Mortgage Loans at any stage during the life 
of the Fund, the payment of the management fee to the new manager of the Participated Mortgage Loans (which may 
be higher if the new manager is not a company within Barclays Group), will rank 3rd in the payment priority order, 
before the payment of the amounts resulting from each settlement of the Interest Swap Agreement, if the new 
manager is not a company within Barclays Group. In such a case, (i) the references made in this Prospectus to the 
items between 3rd and 18th of the payment priority order, will be understood each as made to the items between 4th and 
19th, respectively, (ii) the item relating to the payment to the Issuer of the fee for the management of the Participated 
Mortgage Loans in accordance with the Management Agreement (referred to before as ranked 19th) will be deleted, and 
(iii) the references made in this Prospectus to the items 1st, 2nd and 20th of the payment priority order shall be 
unaffected.  
Likewise, in the event that the initial expenses of incorporation of the Fund and issuance of the Notes and the interest 
corresponding to the payment deferral of the subscription value of the Mortgage Shares were lower than the amount of 
the Initial Expenses Subordinated Loan Agreement, payment of the principal amount of the Initial Expenses 
Subordinated Loan Agreement not allocated to cover said expenses will be in 18th place in the payment priority order. In 
that event, references made in this Prospectus to the items 18th to 20th of the payment priority order shall be 
understood to have been made to items 19th to 21th , respectively.

With the purpose of consolidating its financial structure and of procuring the biggest possible coverage of the inherent 
risks of the issue, the Managing Company, in the name and on behalf of the Fund, will enter into the following 
agreements: 
 
(i)  
Financial Services Agreement with Barclays Bank, S.A., by virtue of which, the amounts deposited by the Fund 
through its Managing Company in the Cash Account opened with Barclays Bank, S.A. will accrue an interest rate 
equal to the monthly average of the EONIA rate, calculated by the European Central Bank and published by 
REUTERS in its page EONIA, corresponding to the previous month (paragraph V.3.1). It also provides for the 
agency of payments of the Notes (paragraph V.4.3). 
 
(ii)  
Initial Expenses Subordinated Loan Agreement with Barclays Bank PLC, Spanish Branch, for an amount of 
1,788,250.92 euros, which will be allocated to financing the expenses of incorporation of the Fund and issue of 
the Notes, to partially finance the subscription of the Mortgage Shares and to finance the interest accrued on 
the nominal of the Mortgage Shares between the Incorporation Date and the Disbursement Date (paragraph 
V.3.2). 
 
(iii)  
Reserve Fund Subordinated Loan Agreement with Barclays Bank PLC, Spanish Branch, for an amount of 
6,300,000 euros, which will be fully allocated to fund the Reserve Fund (paragraph V.3.3). Paragraph V.3.4 
provides for the Reserve Fund. 
 
(iv)  
Interest Swap Agreement with Barclays Bank PLC, Spanish Branch, the purpose of which is to avoid the basis 
risk of floating rate interest which exists in the Fund between the floating rate interest of the Participated 
Mortgage Loans, calculated on the basis of the 12 month Euribor, and the floating rate interest on the Notes, 
calculated on the basis of the 3 month Euribor and with quarterly accrual and settlement -except for the first 
Interest Accrual Period- (paragraph V.3.5) 
 
(v)  
Other agreements, in particular, (a) the Management Agreement of the Participated Mortgage Loans with 
Barclays Bank, S.A. (paragraph V.4.1) and (b) the Underwriting Agreement with the Underwriting Entities, and 
the Underwriting subject to conditions precedent and Arrangement Agreement with Barclays Bank, S.A. 
(paragraph V.4.2).

Annex IV of the Prospectus shows the audit report on the selected portfolio of 
mortgage loans granted by Barclays Bank, S.A., which will mostly be securitised. The 
securitised mortgage loans (the “Participated Mortgage Loans”) will be transferred 
to the Fund through the issue of mortgage shares (hereinafter, the “Mortgage 
Shares”). This audit report has been drawn up by PricewaterhouseCoopers Auditors, 
S.L. with ID number for tax purposes B-79031290, and registered office in Madrid, 
Paseo de la Castellana 43, a company registered with the Official Register of Account 
Auditors under number S-0242. 
The audit report informs on a series of attributes (characteristics), both quantitative 
and qualitative, of the portfolio of the Participated Mortgage Loans and, in particular, 
on the purpose of the loan, the borrower's identification, date of formalisation, 
maturity date, reference interest rate, spread, applied interest rate, initial amount of 
the loan, current balance of the loan, delays in payment, appraisal value, LTV ratio, 
location of the mortgaged property, mortgage guarantee and insurance against 
damages. 
If despite the Issuer’s confirmations and those made by the Auditors, it is detected 
during the life of the Mortgage Shares that any Participated Mortgage Loan underlying 
to them did not fully adhere on the Incorporation Date to the characteristics contained 
in paragraph IV.1.a) of the Prospectus, the Issuer undertakes, in accordance with the 
provisions set forth in paragraph IV.1.d) of the Prospectus, to substitute the 
 
 
20 


 
corresponding Mortgage Share immediately or to repay it, as the case may be. In 
accordance with paragraph IV.1.d), confirmation of the suitability of the replacement 
loan must be given by the  Auditors (or any replacement), prior to the substitution. 
I.4. 
Observations made by the Managing Company 
The Managing Company believes it is necessary to give notice of the unguaranteed 
nature of the principal amount of the Notes that will be paid on each Payment Date, 
because the main characteristic of the Notes resides in that their repayment is directly 
tied to the payments made by the debtors of the Participated Mortgage Loans, 
therefore being directly affected by the evolution, delays, anticipated payments or any 
other related incidents. 
The partial repayment of the Notes will depend on the speed of the repayment of the 
Mortgage Shares. Accordingly, there is no way to predetermine the amounts that will 
be applied to the repayment of the Notes on each Payment Date. 
The early repayment risk will be passed on to the Noteholders on a quarterly basis, on 
each Payment Date, through the partial repayment of the Notes. In any event, 
payments of principal on the Class A1 Notes rank ahead on a timing basis of 
payments of principal on the Class A2 Notes, which, in turn, rank ahead of Class B 
Notes, which, in turn, rank ahead of Class C Notes, and which, in turn, rank ahead of 
Class D Notes (except for the pro rata repayment of the principal amount of Classes 
A2, B, C and D, in accordance with paragraph II.11.3.2 below). 
It is important to note that constant annual rates of prepayment (CPR) have been 
used in the preparation of the Prospectus; these CPR are 5%, 10% and 15%, the 
range which the Managing Company, on behalf of the Fund, believes represents the 
minimum and maximum percentages of probable prepayment. However this range is 
not definitive. Please refer to paragraph II.12.b) of the Prospectus. 
It is also important to note that on the date of registration of this Prospectus the final 
spreads applicable for determination of the Nominal Interest Rate of each Class of 
Notes have not yet been determined. Consequently, the charts and examples included 
in this Prospectus which refer to (or otherwise use) the Nominal Interest Rate of the 
all Classes of Notes have been prepared (except otherwise indicated) by using the 
spreads which the Managing Company will determine on its own in the event that an 
agreement is not reached with the Entidad Directora and the Underwriting Entities on 
the final spreads applicable to each Class of Notes (0.05% for Class A1 Notes, 0.15% 
for Class A2 Notes, 0.26% for Class B Notes, 0.50% for Class C Notes and 1.75% for 
Class D Notes). 
The interest payment of all Classes is subject to the same uncertainty as described for 
the repayment of the principal, since it depends on the payments made by the 
debtors of the Participated Mortgage Loans. However, the payment of interest on the 
Class A1 and A2 Notes is less affected than the payment of interest on Class B Notes, 
which, in turn, is less affected than the payment of interest on Class C Notes, which, 
 
 
21 


 
in turn, is less affected than the payment of interest on Class D Notes, due to the 
subordinated nature of some Classes with respect to other Classes. 
It should be kept in mind that it is fundamental that the periodic information that the 
Managing Company will provide on a quarterly basis to the Noteholders and the CNMV 
is given at the times and in the forms set out in the Prospectus or as determined by 
the CNMV in the future. As a result of this information, containing actual figures rather 
than estimations, both the Noteholders and the CNMV will have a precise knowledge, 
with the abovementioned regularity, of both the evolution of the Mortgage Shares’ 
portfolio (and specifically about any delay in payment greater than ninety (90) days, 
prepayment rates, etc.) and the unpaid balances and percentages that these balances 
represent compared to the initial nominal amount of the Notes.

II.1.2. Information on the requirements and prior resolutions necessary for listing 
on the Stock Exchange or in an organised secondary market 
 
In accordance with article 5.9 of Law 19/1992, immediately after the granting of the 
Incorporation Deed and once the disbursement of the Notes has been completed (as 
referred to in paragraph II.18.5), the Managing Company will request the listing of the 
Notes in the AIAF Fixed-Interest Securities Market (hereinafter, “AIAF”), which is an 
official secondary securities market recognised in the Sixth Temporary Disposition set 
forth in Law 37/1998 of 16 November amending the previous Law 24/1988. It is 
expected that actual listing will take place no later than thirty (30) days following the 
Disbursement Date (as defined in paragraph II.18.5). 
 
In the event that the listing of the Notes in the AIAF is not completed within the 
above period, the Managing Company will immediately inform the Noteholders and 
will specify the reasons, by means of an announcement published in a newspaper that 
is distributed nation-wide, in accordance with the provisions of paragraph III.5.3.b) 
and c).  Such actions shall be without prejudice to the contractual liability of the 
 
 
24 


 
Managing Company that could result from the listing of the Notes in the AIAF not 
being completed within the above period. 
 
Additionally, the Managing Company will request, on behalf of the Fund, the inclusion 
of the Notes in the Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de Registro, Compensación y 
Liquidación de Valores, S.A. in order for the clearing and settlement of the Notes to be 
carried out in accordance with the Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de Registro, 
Compensación y Liquidación de Valores, S.A. operating rules (existing as of the date 
hereof or which may be approved in the future) with respect to securities listed in the 
AIAF and represented by book entries. 
 
Furthermore, application will be made by the Financial Agent for the Notes to be 
accepted for clearing and settlement through Clearstream Banking Sociète Anonyme, 
Luxembourg.

Evaluation of the risk inherent in the securities issued by the Fund, carried

evaluated by a rating entity recognised by the CNMV. 
 
The Managing Company has entrusted the evaluation of the credit risk of the Notes to 
Standard & Poor’s España, S.A. (“S&P”), Moody’s Investors Service España, S.A. 
(“Moody’s”) and Fitch Ratings España, S.A. (“Fitch”) (together, hereinafter, the 
“Rating Agencies”), which are rating entities recognised by the CNMV for the 
purposes set forth in article 5.8 of Law 19/1992. 
 
Rating granted to the issue of the Notes 
 
Prior to the date of registration of this Prospectus, S&P assigned an AAA rating to the 
Class A1 and Class A2 Notes, an A rating to the Class B Notes, a BBB rating to the 
Class C Notes and a BB rating to the Class D Notes, all on a provisional basis. It is 
expected that the above ratings will be confirmed as final ratings by such Rating 
Agency prior to the commencement of the Subscription Period (referred to in 
paragraph II.18.3 of the Prospectus). 
 
 
25 


 
 
Prior to the date of registration of this Prospectus, Moody’s assigned an Aaa rating to 
the Class A1 and A2 Notes, an Aa3 rating to the Class B Notes, a Baa1 rating to the 
Class C Notes, and a Ba1 rating to Class D Notes, all on a provisional basis. It is 
expected that the above ratings will be confirmed as final ratings by such Rating 
Agency prior to the commencement of the Subscription Period (referred to in 
paragraph II.18.3 of the Prospectus). 
 
Prior to the date of registration of this Prospectus, Fitch assigned an AAA rating to the 
Class A1 and Class A2 Notes, an AA- rating to the Class B Notes, a BBB+ rating to the 
Class C Notes and a BB+ rating to the Class D Notes, all on a provisional basis. It is 
expected that the above ratings will be confirmed as final ratings by such Rating 
Agency prior to the commencement of the Subscription Period (referred to in 
paragraph II.18.3 of the Prospectus). 
 
Failure to confirm any of the above provisional ratings prior to the commencement of 
the Subscription Period would constitute a termination event in respect of the 
incorporation of the Fund and the issue of the Mortgage Shares and the Notes.  
The above will be immediately communicated to the CNMV and will be disclosed to 
the public as provided in paragraph III.5.3.b)2. 
 
A copy of the letters confirming the provisional ratings issued by S&P, Moody’s and 
Fitch with respect to the Notes is attached as Annex III.

The description of the meaning given by S&P to its long-term and short-term ratings 
referred to in this Prospectus is the following:  
 
S&P Long-term 
AAA 
An obligation rated “AAA” has the highest rating assigned by S&P. The 
obligor's capacity to meet its financial commitment on the obligation is extremely 
strong. 
 
AA 
An obligation rated “AA” differs from the highest-rated obligations only in 
small degree. The obligor´s capacity to meet its financial commitment on the 
obligation is still strong. 
 
A 
An obligation rated “A” is somewhat more susceptible to the adverse effects 
of changes in circumstances and economic conditions than obligations in higher rated 
 
 
27 


 
categories. However, the obligor's capacity to meet its financial commitment on the 
obligation is still strong. 
 
BBB 
An obligation rated “BBB” exhibits adequate protection parametres. 
However, adverse economic conditions changing circumstances are more likely to lead 
to a weakened capacity of the obligor to meet its financial commitment on the 
obligation. 
 
BB  
An obligation rated “BB” is less vulnerable to nonpayment than other 
speculative issues. However, it faces notorial ongoing uncertainties or exposure to 
adverse business, financial, or economic conditions, which could lead to the obligor´s 
inadequate capacity to meet its financial commitment on the obligation. 
 
The ratings from “AA” to “CCC” may be modified by the addition of a plus or minus 
sign to show relative standing within the major rating categories.  
S&P Short-term 
A-1 
A short-term obligation rated “A-1” is rated in the highest category by S&P. 
The obligor's capacity to meet its financial commitment on the obligation is strong. 
Within this category, certain obligations are designated with a plus sign (+). This 
indicates that the obligor's capacity to meet its financial commitment on these 
obligations is extremely strong.  
Additionally, the description of the meaning given by Moody’s to its long-term and 
short-term ratings referred to in this Prospectus is the following: 
Moody’s Long-term 
Aaa 
Notes which are rated “Aaa” are judged to be of the best quality. They carry 
the smallest degree of investment risk and are generally referred to as "gilt edged." 
Interest payments are protected by a large or by an exceptionally stable margin and 
principal is secure. 
Aa 
Notes which are rated “Aa” are judged to be of high quality by all standards. 
Together with the “Aaa” group they comprise what are generally known as high-grade 
bonds. They are rated lower than the best bonds because margins of protection may 
not be as large as in “Aaa” securities or fluctuation of protective elements may be of 
greater amplitude or there may be other elements present which make the long-term 
risk appear somewhat larger than the “Aaa” securities. 
A 
Notes which are rated “A” possess many favourable investment attributes 
and are to be considered as upper-medium-grade obligations. Factors giving security 
to principal and interest are considered adequate, but elements may be present which 
suggest a susceptibility to impairment some time in the future. 
 
 
28 


 
Baa 
Notes which are rated “Baa” are considered as medium-grade obligations. 
Interest payments and principal security appear adequate for the present but certain 
protective elements may be lacking or may be characteristically unreliable over any 
great length of time. Such notes lack outstanding investment characteristics and in 
fact have speculative characteristics as well. 
Ba 
Notes which are rated “Ba” are judge to have speculative elements: their 
future cannot be considered as well-assured. Often the protection of interest and 
principal payments may be very moderate, and thereby not well safeguarded during 
both good and bad times over the future. Uncertainty of position characterizes bonds 
in this class. 
Moody’s applies numerical modifiers 1, 2, and 3 in each generic rating classification 
from “Aa” through “Caa”. The modifier 1 indicates that the obligation ranks in the 
higher end of its generic rating category; the modifier 2 indicates a mid-range 
ranking; and the modifier 3 indicates a ranking in the lower end of that generic rating 
category.  
Moody’s Short-term 
P-1 Superior ability for repayment of senior short-term debt obligations. 
P-2 
Strong ability for repayment of senior short-term debt obligations. 
Additionally, the description of the meaning given by Fitch to its long-term and short-
term ratings referred to in this Prospectus is the following: 
Fitch Long-term 
AAA  “AAA” rating assigned by Fitch denotes the highest credit quality. It is assigned 
only in case of exceptionally strong capacity to timely payment of principal and 
interest of the financial obligations. This capacity is highly unlikely to be adversely 
affected by foreseeable events. 
AA  
“AA” rating assigned by Fitch denotes a very high credit quality. It indicates a 
very strong capacity for timely payment of principal and interest. This capacity is not 
significantly vulnerable to foreseeable events.   
A  
“A” rating assigned by Fitch denotes a high credit quality. The capacity for 
timely repayment of principal and interest is strong. This capacity may, nevertheless, 
be more vulnerable to changes in circumstances or in economic conditions than in the 
case of higher ratings. 
BBB “BBB” rating assigned by Fitch indicates that there is currently a low 
expectation of credit risk. The capacity for timely payment of financial commitments is 
considered adequate, but adverse changes in circumstances and in economic 
 
 
29 


 
conditions are more likely to impair this capacity. This is the lowest investment-grade 
category. 
BB 
“BB” rating assigned by Fitch indicates that there is a possibility of credit risk 
developing, particularly as the result of economic change over the time; however, 
business or financial alternatives may be available to allow financial commitments to 
be met. Securities rated in this category are not investment grade.  
Fitch Short-term 
F1  
“F1” rating assigned by Fitch denotes the highest credit quality. It indicates the 
strongest capacity for timely payment of principal and interest. It may have and 
added “+” to denote any exceptionally strong credit feature.  
Notes to long-term and short-term ratings “+” or “-” may be added to a rating to 
denote relative status within major rating categories. Such suffixes are not added to 
the “AAA” long-term rating category, to categories below “CCC”, or to short-term 
ratings other than “F1”. 
The ratings assigned to each of the Classes of Notes by S&P measure the Fund´s 
ability to meet payments of interest as they fall due on each set Payment Date and 
repayment of the principal throughout the life of the transaction and, in any event, 
before the Final Maturity Date. 
The ratings assigned to each of the Classes of Notes by Moody´s measure the 
expected loss before the Final Maturity Date. In Moody´s opinion, the structure allows 
timely payment of interest and payment of principal during the life of the transaction 
and, in any event, before the Final Maturity Date. 
Finally, the ratings assigned to each of the Classes of Notes by Fitch measure the 
Fund´s ability to meet payments of interest as they fall due on each set Payment Date 
and repayment of the principal throughout the life of the transaction and, in any 
event, before the Final Maturity Date,, in accordance with the terms of this Prospectus 
for Classes of Notes and the rest of ancillary documentation, which provide for the 
deferral of payment of interest on Class B, C and D Notes in the event that some 
circumstances established in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules 
established in paragraph V.5.2 occur. This may imply that, while these circumstances 
resulting in the deferral of payment of interest on Class B, C and D Notes occur, 
interest may be unpaid on a given Payment Date if the Fund has not sufficient 
liquidity. Such unpaid interest will be paid on the following Payment Date on which 
the Fund has enough liquidity (paragraph II.10).  
The rating takes into account the structure of the Notes issued, their legal aspects and 
those of the Fund which has issued such Notes, the characteristics of the Participated 
Mortgage Loans and the cash flows of the structure. 
 
 
30 


 
The rating does not evaluate the probability that the mortgagors may carry out any 
early repayment of the principal amount or to what extent such early repayment may 
differ from what was originally expected. The rating does not consist, by any means, 
of a rating of the level of actual returns. 
The assigned rating, as well as any review or suspension of it: 
(i) 
is issued by the Rating Agencies on the basis of the large amount of 
information they receive and, since they do not guarantee the accuracy or 
completeness of such information,  the Rating Agencies cannot be considered in any 
way responsible for such information; and  
(ii) 
does not constitute and may under no circumstances be interpreted as an 
invitation, recommendation or inducement directed to the investors for them to carry 
out any type of operation regarding the Notes and particularly, to purchase, hold, 
encumber or sell such Notes. 
The ratings may be reviewed, suspended or withdrawn at any time by the Rating 
Agencies by reason of any information which may come to their notice. Such 
situations, which will not constitute a reason for early repayment of the Fund, will be 
immediately informed to both the CNMV and the Noteholders, in accordance with 
provisions set forth in paragraph III.5.3. 
To carry out the process of rating and follow up, the Rating Agencies rely on the 
accuracy and completeness of the information provided by the Managing Company, 
the auditors, the lawyers and other experts. 
The Managing Company undertakes, on behalf of the Fund, to provide the Rating 
Agencies with regular information on the situation of the Fund and the performance of 
the Mortgage Shares. Likewise it will provide such information when reasonably 
required to do so and always when there is a change in the conditions either of the 
Fund or the agreements entered into by the Fund through its Managing Company or 
the concerned parties. In any case, within thirty (30) days from each Payment Date, 
the Managing Company, in the name and on behalf of the Fund, shall provide to the 
Rating Agencies the information referred to in the form attached to this Prospectus as 
Annex VII.  
The Managing Company will use its best efforts to maintain the rating of the Notes at 
its initial level and, in the event that this rating drops, it will use its best efforts to 
recover it. 
II.4. 
Nature and name of the securities which are offered with an indication of 
the issue or tranche number 
The total amount of the issue of Notes amounts to a nominal amount of SEVEN 
HUNDRED MILLION EUROS (700,000,000 €) and is composed of SEVEN 
 
 
31 


 
THOUSAND (7,000) Notes. This nominal amount is divided into five Classes of 
Notes: 
(i) 
Senior notes which make up Class A1 (“Class A1 Notes”) for a total 
nominal amount of ONE HUNDRED AND FIFTY FOUR MILLION EUROS 
(154,000,000 €), comprised of ONE THOUSAND, FIVE HUNDRED AND FORTY 
(1,540) senior Notes having each a face value of ONE HUNDRED THOUSAND 
EUROS (100,000 €), represented through book entries. 
(ii) 
Senior notes which make up Class A2 (“Class A2 Notes”) for a total 
nominal amount of FIVE HUNDRED AND TWENTY FOUR MILLION EUROS 
(524,00,000 €), comprised of FIVE THOUSAND, TWO HUNDRED FORTY 
(5,240) senior Notes having each a face value of ONE HUNDRED THOUSAND 
EUROS (100,000 €), represented through book entries. 
(iii) 
Subordinated notes which make up Class B (“Class B Notes”) for a total 
nominal amount of SEVEN MILLION EUROS (7,000,000 €), comprised of 
SEVENTY (70) Notes having each a face value of ONE HUNDRED THOUSAND 
EUROS (100,000 €), represented through book entries. 
(iv) 
Subordinated notes which make up Class C (“Class C Notes”) for a total 
nominal amount of SEVEN MILLION SEVEN HUNDRED THOUSAND EUROS 
(7,700,000 €), comprised of SEVENTY SEVEN (77) Notes having each a face value 
of ONE HUNDRED THOUSAND EUROS (100,000 €), represented through book 
entries. 
(v) 
Subordinated notes which make up Class D (“Class D Notes”) for a total 
nominal amount of SEVEN MILLION THREE HUNDRED THOUSAND EUROS 
(7,300,000 €), comprised of SEVENTY THREE (73) Notes having each a face value 
of ONE HUNDRED THOUSAND EUROS (100,000 €), represented through book 
entries. 
The repayment of the principal amount of Class A2 Notes are subordinated with 
regard to the Class A1 Notes, whereas the interest of both Series will be paid on a 
pro-rata basis. The repayment of the principal amount and payment of interest of 
Class B Notes are subordinated with regard to the Class A2 Notes, whereas the 
repayment of the principal amount and interest of the Class C Notes is subordinated 
with regard to the Class B Notes, and the repayment of the principal amount and 
interest of Class D Notes is subordinated with regard to the Class C Notes (except for 
the pro rata repayment of the principal amount of Classes A2, B, C and D in 
accordance with paragraph II.11.3.2), in accordance with the payment priority order 
contained in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules established in paragraph 
V.5.2. and the payment priority order in the event of liquidation of the Fund contained 
in paragraph V.6.1. and the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
 
 
32 


 
Subscription for or possession of the Notes of one Class does not entail the 
subscription for or possession of the Notes of the other Class. 
The Notes are governed by Law 19/1992, having the legal status of fixed income 
securities, homogeneous and standardised, eligible for trading in organised securities 
markets. Therefore, the Fund possesses a legal and different financial configuration to 
that of investment funds. 
II.4.1. Legal regime governing the securities, with specification of the procedures 
which guarantee the certainty and effectiveness of the rights of the first 
and subsequent holders. Implications that produce the mandatory 
connection between the timetable for payment of the principal amount  and 
interest of such securities and the flow of revenues and collections 
resulting from the assets that are securitised through the Fund, for the 
financial service of each issue of notes issued by the Fund 
The Notes are governed by Law 19/1992 of July 7, on the Regime applicable to 
Companies and Funds of Real Estate Investment and on Funds of Mortgage 
Securitisation. 
The Noteholders will be identified as such in accordance with the accounting records 
kept by the Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de Registro, Compensación y 
Liquidación de Valores, S A., as provided in paragraph II.5. Ownership certificates 
may be issued at the Noteholder’s request and at its expense in accordance with the 
provisions set forth in the fourth section of Chapter 1 of Title I of Royal Decree 
116/1992, of 14 February on the representation of securities through book entries and 
clearing and settlement of stock market transactions (“Royal Decree 116/1992”). 
.
The Notes may be freely transferred by any means permitted by law. The ownership 
of each Note will be transferred through an accounting record transfer. The 
registration of the transfer in favour of the purchaser in the accounting record will 
produce the same effects as delivery of the security were title to the security capable 
of being transferred by delivery and from that moment on, the transfer will be 
effective vis-a-vis third parties. 
The Managing Company, acting on behalf of the Fund, will enter into a “Financial 
Services Agreement” with Barclays Bank, S.A. (hereinafter, and for these purposes, 
the "Financial Agent") whereby the Managing Company shall invest the amounts 
received on behalf of the Fund in a Cash Account opened with the Financial Agent in 
the name of the Fund. The balance of the Cash Account shall accrue interest at a 
monthly average of EONIA interest rate (Euro Overnight Interest Average), calculated 
by the European Central Bank and published by REUTERS in its page EONIA, 
corresponding to the previous month, whilst the credit rating of the non-subordinated 
and unsecured short-term debt of Barclays Bank PLC at any moment in time is not 
lower than A-1, P-1 or F1 (its current ratings being A-1+, P-1 and F1+), according to 
the rating scales for short-term risks of S&P, Moody’s and Fitch, respectively, and the 
 
 
33 


 
shareholding of Barclays Bank PLC in the Financial Agent is equal to or exceeds of 
51%. In the event that any of the above referred credit ratings is reduced or if the 
shareholding of Barclays Bank PLC in the Financial Agent falls below the above-
mentioned percentage, then the Financial Agent, within thirty (30) Business Days from 
the assignment of this lower rating or from the reduction of Barclays Bank PLC’s 
holding in the Financial Agent below the above mentioned percentage: 
(a) 
shall obtain from a credit entity with a short-term risk rating of at least A-1, 
P-1 and F1 (in accordance with S&P, Moody’s and Fitch short-term debt rating scales, 
respectively), a joint and several first demand guarantee as security for the amounts 
deposited in the Cash Account, or 
(b) 
shall transfer the Cash Account of the Fund to an entity with a non-
subordinated and unsecured short-term debt of at least A-1, P-1 and F1 ratings (in 
accordance with S&P, Moody’s and Fitch short-term debt rating scales, respectively), 
arranging for the best obtainable return of the balances of the Cash Account, or 
(c) 
if options a) and b) above are not possible, the Managing Company shall 
obtain from the Financial Agent or a third party collateral security in favour of the 
Fund on financial assets with a credit rating of not less than that of the Spanish State 
Government Debt (“Deuda Pública del Es ado Español”), in an amount sufficient to 
guarantee the commitments established in the Financial Services Agreement, or 
t
(d) 
if none of the above-mentioned measures may be achieved, the Managing 
Company will replace the Financial Agent with another credit entity with a short-term 
debt rating of at least A-1, P-1 and F1 (in accordance with S&P, Moody’s and Fitch 
short-term debt rating scales, respectively), obtaining the best obtainable return of 
the balances of the Cash Account. 
In event (b) above, the Managing Company will subsequently transfer the balances of 
the Cash Account back to the Financial Agent, provided that the non-subordinated and 
unsecured short-term debt of Barclays Bank PLC is assigned the aforementioned A-1, 
P-1 and F1 ratings and the stake held by Barclays Bank PLC in the Financial Agent is 
equal or higher than 51%.  
The substitution of the Financial Agent will in no event negatively affect the ratings of 
the Notes. 
Likewise, in the event that the ratings on the non-subordinated and unsecured short-
term debt of Barclays Bank PLC falls to A-1 (in accordance with S&P short-term debt 
rating scale), if the balance of the Cash Account exceeds 20% of the Unpaid Principal 
Balance of the Notes on a given Payment Date, the Managing Company will deposit 
the difference on an account (the “Excess Balance Account”) opened by the 
Managing Company in another credit entity whose short-term debt is assigned a 
minimum rating of A-1+ (in accordance the aforementioned rating scale), arranging 
for the best obtainable return of such balance. 
 
 
34 


 
Similarly, in the event that the non-subordinated and unsecured short-term debt of 
Barclays Bank PLC attains again the A-1+ rating (in accordance with S&P short-term 
debt rating scale), the Managing Company will subsequently transfer to the Cash 
Account opened with the Financial Agent the then balance of the Excess Balance 
Account.  
II.4.2. Other implications and risks that, due to the legal and economic nature of 
the assets which are grouped together in the Fund, might affect  the 
financial servicing of the securities issued by the Fund as a result of the 
securitisation of such assets 
a) 
Risk of non-payment of the Mortgage Shares 
In accordance with article 5.8 of Law 19/1992, the risk of non-payment of the 
Mortgage Shares shall be borne by the Noteholders.  
As a result, the Issuer will assume no responsibility for any default of payment by the 
mortgagors, whether of principal, interest or any other amounts which might be owed 
by such mortgagors under the Participated Mortgage Loans. It will also assume no 
responsibility for ensuring, directly or indirectly, the successful completion of the 
transaction nor will it grant any backing or guarantee, or enter into any repurchase 
agreement in connection with the Mortgage Shares, save for those which did not 
comply on the Incorporation Date with the conditions and characteristics contained in 
paragraph IV.1.a) of the Prospectus and in accordance with the provisions set forth 
therein. 
b) 
Risk of early repayment of the Mortgage Shares 
Through the issue of Mortgage Shares, the Issuer, in the terms described in  Chapter 
IV of the Prospectus, allows the Fund to participate in the principal and interest of the 
Participated Mortgage Loans granted by the Issuer. 
The Mortgage Shares contained in the Fund are open to early repayment when 
borrowers of the Participated Mortgage Loans prepay part of the capital pending 
amortisation, in the terms set out in each of the relevant loan deeds.  Similarly, the 
Mortgage Shares will be amortised entirely in the event the Issuer is substituted 
(subrogated) in the relevant Participated Mortgage Loans by other financial entities, 
subject to Law 2/1994, of March 30, on Subrogation and Amendment of Mortgage 
Loans, as amended, among others, by Royal Decree-Law 2/2003, of April 25 ("Law 
2/1994"). 
The risk of early repayment will be transferred on a quarterly basis, on each Payment 
Date, to the Noteholders through their partial repayment in accordance with the 
provisions set forth in paragraph II.11.3.2 of the Prospectus. 
c) 
Limited Protection  
 
 
35 


 
 
An investment in the Notes could be affected, among other things, by a deterioration 
in general economical conditions that shall produce a negative effect on the payments 
of the Participated Mortgage Loans which support the Issue of Notes by the Fund. In 
the event that there are significant levels of default defaults on payments of 
Participated Mortgage Loans, the limited protection against losses in the portfolio of 
Participated Mortgage Loans which results from the credit enhancement described in 
paragraph V.3 of the Prospectus may be reduced or even lost. Furthermore, the level 
of subordination in payments of interest and repayment of principal of some Classes 
of Notes with regard to other Classes of Notes allows more senior Classes to have 
greater protection than more junior Classes. 
 
d) 
Liquidity 
 
There is no assurance that the Notes will be traded on the market with a minimum 
frequency or volume. 
 
There is no commitment of any entity to trade in the secondary market in order to 
give liquidity to the Notes by offering a counterparty. 
 
In no case shall the Fund repurchase the Notes from the Noteholders, although the 
Notes may be early and totally repaid in the event of Early Liquidation of the Fund, as 
set out in paragraph III.8.1 of the Prospectus. 
 
e)  
Profitability 
 
The fulfilment of the repayment of the Participated Mortgage Loans is affected by a 
variety of geographical, economic and social factors such as seasonality, market 
interest rates, the economic and labour situation of the Debtors and the general 
economic circumstances, which avoid its foresee-ability. 
 
The calculation of the Internal Rate of Return, of the average life and maturity of the 
Notes included in the Prospectus is based on several hypothesis, such as early 
repayment rates and non-payment rates of the Participated Mortgage Loans which 
may not become true, as well as on future market interest rates, due to the fact that 
the nominal interest rate of each Class is variable. 
 
f)  
Lack of actions 
 
The Noteholders and the remaining creditors of the Fund shall have no action against 
the Debtors of the Participated Mortgage Loans that have not fulfilled their payment 
obligations, being the Managing Company, as representative of the Fund, the holder 
of such actions. 
 
 
 
36 


 
The Noteholders and the remaining creditors of the Fund shall have no action against 
the Fund or the Managing Company in the event of payment default of the Fund 
which arises from early repayment of non-payment of the Mortgage Shares, in the 
event of default of the counterparties of the transactions entered into in the name and 
on behalf of the Fund or because of non-sufficiency of the financial operations of 
coverage to comply with the payment obligations of the Notes of each Class. 
 
The Noteholders and the remaining creditors of the Fund shall not have other action 
against the issuer of the Mortgage Shares or the Managing Company, respectively, 
than those arising from non-fulfilment of their respective duties and, consequently, 
never as a result of non-payment or early repayment.  
 
II.5. 
Form of representation and name and address of the entity in charge of its 
accounting record 
The Notes will be represented by means of book entries in accordance with article 5.9 
of Law 19/1992 and will be incorporated as such by means of their registration in the 
relevant accounting record. The Incorporation Deed will have the effects set forth in 
article 6 of Law 24/1988. 
The name, number of units, face value and other characteristics and conditions 
necessary for the identification of the Notes represented by means of book entries will 
be those which are included in the Incorporation Deed and in this Chapter II. 
The Noteholders will be identified as such through the accounting record kept by the 
entities participating in the Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de Registro, 
Compensación y Liquidación de Valores, S.A., which will be appointed in the 
Incorporation Deed as the entity in charge of the accounting records of the Notes, in 
such a way that the clearing and settlement of the Notes is carried out in accordance 
with the operating rules which may have been established or may be established in 
the future by the Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de Registro, Compensación y 
Liquidación de Valores, S.A. with regard to the securities which are listed in AIAF and 
represented through book entries. 
Furthermore, application will be made by the Financial Agent for the Notes to be 
accepted for clearing and settlement through Clearstream Banking Sociète Anonyme, 
Luxembourg.  
The registered office of the Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de Registro, 
Compensación y Liquidación de Valores, S.A. is located in Madrid, Pedro Teixeira 8, 
28020.

 (i) 
Senior notes which make up Class A1 for a total nominal amount of ONE

(iii) 
Subordinated notes which make up Class B for a total nominal amount of 
SEVEN MILLION EUROS (7,000,000 €), comprised of SEVENTY (70) Notes 
having each a face value of ONE HUNDRED THOUSAND EUROS (100,000 €), 
represented through book entries. 
(iv) 
Subordinated notes which make up Class C for a total nominal amount of 
SEVEN MILLION SEVEN HUNDRED THOUSAND EUROS (7,700,000 €), 
comprised of SEVENTY SEVEN (77) Notes having each a face value of ONE 
HUNDRED THOUSAND EUROS (100,000 €), represented through book entries. 
 (v) 
Subordinated notes which make up Class D for a total nominal amount of 
SEVEN MILLION THREE HUNDRED THOUSAND EUROS (7,300,000 €), 
comprised of SEVENTY THREE (73) Notes having each a face value of ONE 
HUNDRED THOUSAND EUROS (100,000 €), represented through book entries. 
The repayment of the principal amount of Class A2 Notes is subordinated with regard 
to the Class A1 Notes, whereas the interest of both Series will be paid on a pro-rata 
basis. The repayment of the principal amount and payment of interest of Class B 
Notes are subordinated with regard to the Class A2 Notes, whereas the repayment of 
the principal amount and interest of Class C Notes are subordinated with regard to the 
Class B, and Class D Notes with regard to the Class C Notes (except for the pro rata 
repayment of the principal amount of Classes A2, B, C and D in accordance with 
paragraph II.11.3.2), in accordance with the payment priority order contained in 
paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.5.2. and the 
payment priority order in the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph 
V.6.1. and the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
 
 
38 


 
Subscription for or possession of the Notes of one Class does not require or entail the 
subscription or possession of Notes of another Class. 
II.7. 
Face and effective value of each security showing, if applicable, the 
premium expressed in proportion to the face value and in monetary units 
per security. Currency used to express each one of the Classes of securities 
which are issued by the Fund 
The issue of Notes is comprised of five (5) Classes denominated in euros: the Class A1 
Notes, A2 Notes, B Notes, C Notes and D Notes. 
The issue price of Notes for all Classes will be one hundred thousand (100,000) euros 
per Note, free of subscription expenses for the subscriber. The Notes are issued at 
100% of their nominal amount. 
The expenses inherent in the subscription of Notes will be borne by the Fund. 
The reimbursement price for the Notes will be one hundred thousand (100,000) euros 
per Note, which is equivalent to their nominal amount, free of expenses for the 
Noteholder and payable in instalments on each Payment Date. 
II.8. 
Commissions and related expenses of all kinds which must be mandatorily 
borne by the investors upon subscription to the securities issued by the 
Fund 
The price of subscription set forth in paragraph II.7 above will be free of subscription 
expenses for the subscriber. 
II.9. 
Reference, if applicable, to the existence, as the case may be, of 
commissions to be paid by the holders of the securities issued by the Fund 
and which must be obligatorily represented through book entries, by way of 
registration and maintenance of balance 
The expenses incurred in the registration of the Notes in the accounting records of the 
Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de Registro, Compensación y Liquidación de 
Valores, S.A. will be borne by the Fund, and will not be charged to the Noteholders.  
The entities participating in the Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de Registro, 
Compensación y Liquidación de Valores, S.A. may establish, in accordance with the 
legislation currently in force, the commissions and expenses to be charged to the 
Noteholder by reason of management of securities which they may freely determine 
and which may have been communicated to the Banco de España or the CNMV, as 
their supervising bodies, from time to time. 
II.10. 
Interest rate clause 
II.10.1. Nominal interest rate 
All Classes of Notes will bear an annual nominal interest rate, which may be varied 
quarterly and is payable on a quarterly basis.  
 
 
39 


 
The annual nominal interest rate (hereinafter, the “Nominal Interest Rate”) will be 
paid on a quarterly basis on each Payment Date, on the Unpaid Principal Balance of 
the Notes of each Class (both concepts are described below, in paragraphs II.10.3 
and II.11.3.2.3, respectively) provided that the Fund has sufficient liquidity in 
accordance with the payment priority order set out in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the 
exceptional rules provided in paragraph V.5.2. and the payment priority order in the 
event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph V.6.1. and the exceptional 
rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
The withholdings, levies, duties and taxes already established or to be established in 
the future on capital, interest or returns of the Notes, will be solely borne by the 
Noteholders and their value will be calculated, as the case may be, by the Managing 
Company, in the name and on behalf of the Fund, in the manner established by law. 
a) 
Accrued interest 
The duration of the issue will be divided into successive “Interest Accrual Periods” 
which will include the effective days elapsed between each Payment Date, the initial 
Payment Date being included in each Interest Accrual Period and the final Payment 
Date being excluded, in accordance with the general regime and the exceptions set 
forth in paragraph II.10.3. Exceptionally, the first Interest Accrual Period will have a 
duration other than three months and equivalent to the time elapsed between the 
Disbursement Date (inclusive) and the first Payment Date (exclusive), being calculated 
on the basis of a year of 360 days in both cases. 
b) 
Nominal Interest rate 
The Nominal Interest Rate for each Interest Accrual Period will be that resulting from 
adding (i) the reference interest rate or, if required, its substitute, both described in 
paragraph c) below, and (ii) a spread for each Class: 
• Class A1: spread ranging between 0.02% and 0.10%, both inclusive. 
• Class A2: spread ranging between 0.10% and 0.20%, both inclusive. 
• Class B: spread ranging between 0.16% and 0.36%, both inclusive. 
• Class C: spread ranging between 0.30% and 0.70%, both inclusive. 
• Class D: spread ranging between 1.25% and 2.25%. both inclusive. 
The spread applicable to each Class of Notes, expressed as a percentage, shall be 
determined by the Managing Company, with, to the extent possible, the prior 
agreement of the Entidad Directora and the Underwriting Entities, before 11:00 hours 
(CET) of the day of commencement of the Subscription Period. 
The final spreads applicable to each Class of Notes shall be notified in written form by 
the Managing Company, before the commencement of the Subscription Period, to the 
 
 
40 


 
Entidad Directora and the Underwriting Entities, for notification to potential investors 
which may be interested in subscribing the Notes. The Managing Company shall also 
notify the CNMV as additional information to this Prospectus. 
The final spreads applicable to each Class of Notes shall be included in the notarial 
deed of disbursement of the Notes. 
In the event that an agreement is not reached with the Entidad Directora and the 
Underwriting Entities, the Managing Company will determine the following final 
spreads on its own: 
• Class A1: spread of 0.05%. 
• Class A2: spread of 0.15%. 
• Class B: spread of 0.26%. 
• Class C: spread of 0.50%. 
• Class D: spread of 1.75%. 
c) 
Calculation of the reference Euribor interest rate 
(i) 
The reference interest rate for the determination of the applicable interest 
rate of the Notes will be, for the first Interest Accrual Period, the interpolation of the 
four (4) month Euribor interest rate “Euro InterBank Offered Rate” and the five (5) 
month Euribor interest rate and, for all other Interest Accrual Periods, the three (3) 
months Euribor interest rate, in each case, calculated and distributed by the financial 
information system BRIDGE by order of the FBE ("Federation Bancaire de l’Union 
Europeene"), as determined at 11 hours in the morning (CET time, “Central European 
Time”) on the Interest Rate Fixing Date, described in paragraph d) below, which is 
presently published in the EURIBOR01 electronic pages, supplied by Reuters, and 248, 
supplied by Dow Jones Markets (Bridge Telerate), or any other substitute page which 
may provide these services in the future. 
The above mentioned interpolation shall take into account the number of days 
elapsed from (and including) the Disbursement Date (as defined in paragraph II.18.5 
below) to (but excluding) the first Payment Date. 
The calculation of the above referred interpolation shall be made as follows: 
TCa = (TL - TC) /( DL - DC) x (DCa - DC) + TC 
Where: 
TCa 
is the interest rate resulting from the interpolation, expressed in percentage; 
TL 
is the interest rate of the long period (5 months), expressed in percentage; 
 
 
41 


 
TC 
is the interest rate of the short period (4 months), expressed in percentage; 
DL 
is the number of days of the long period (150 days); 
DC 
is the number of days of the short period (120 days); and  
DCa 
is the number of days elapsed from the Disbursement Date (included) to the 
first Payment Date (excluded). 
The investor may find an example of the application of this interpolation method in 
paragraph II.12.a) below. 
The Euribor interest rate is currently the interest rate offered for interbanking deposits 
in euros, calculated on the basis of the daily average quotation supplied by a panel 
composed of 57 banks, which are among the most active banks in the Euro Zone. The 
interest rate is quoted on the basis of the number of real days up to the date of 
maturity and the year being composed for 360 days and is fixed at 11:00 hours in the 
morning (CET time) and expressed to three (3) decimal places. 
(ii) 
In the event that the interest rate set forth in the above paragraph (i) would 
be impossible to obtain or in the absence of this interest rate, the substitute reference 
interest rate will be the interest rate resulting from calculating the simple arithmetic 
mean of the interbanking interest rates offered for operations of non-transferable 
deposits in euros with three (3) months or, if in respect of the first Interest Accrual 
Period, between four (4) and five (5) months maturity, on the Interest Rate Fixing 
Date, which may be quoted by the banks listed below (the “Reference Banks”) upon 
request from the Managing Company through the Financial Agent. 
¾ 
Banco Bilbao Vizcaya Argentaria, S.A. 
¾ 
Banco Santander Central Hispano, S.A. 
¾ 
Confederación Española de Cajas de Ahorros 
¾ 
Deutsche Bank AG 
In the event that the above substitutive reference interest rate was impossible to 
apply due to a continuous failure to supply the quotation statement by any of the 
above Reference Banks, the interest rate to be applied will be that resulting from 
applying the simple arithmetic mean of the interest rates stated by those Reference 
Banks offering interest rates provided that at least two (2) Reference Banks provide 
interest rates. 
iii) 
In case of absence or impossibility of obtaining the interest rates provided in 
paragraphs (i) and (ii) above, the interest rate to be applied will be the last reference 
interest rate applied to the last Interest Accrual Period and so on for the subsequent 
Interest Accrual Periods for as long as this situation continues. As for the first Interest 
Accrual Period, the above mentioned interpolation shall be made with the latest four 
(4) month Euribor interest rate and five (5) month Euribor interest rate available 
 
 
42 


 
immediately before 11:00 hours in the morning (CET time) on the Interest Rate Fixing 
Date calculated and distributed as described in paragraph (i) above. 
The Managing Company will keep the listings with the content of the EURIBOR01 of 
Reuters and 248 of Telerate screens or, as the case may be, the quotation statements 
of the Reference Banks, as documents evidencing the applied Euribor rate. 
d) 
Interest Rate Fixing Date 
Except for the first Interest Accrual Period, the Nominal Interest Rate applicable to all 
Classes of Notes for each Interest Accrual Period will be determined by the Managing 
Company, in the name and on behalf of the Fund, at 11:00 hours (CET) of the second 
Business Day preceding each Payment Date (hereinafter "Interest Rate Fixing 
Date").  This rate will be applicable to the next Interest Accrual Period. 
The reference interest rate for the first Interest Accrual Period will be determined at 
11:00 hours (CET) of the Incorporation Date, while the Nominal Interest Rate of all 
Classes of Notes for the first Interest Accrual Period will be determined before 11:00 
hours (CET) of the day of commencement of the Subscription Period (once the final 
spreads are fixed), and it will be notified in written form by the Managing Company, 
before the commencement of the Subscription Period, to the Entidad Directora and 
the Underwriting Entities, for notification to potential investors which may be 
interested in subscribing the Notes. Additionally, the Managing Company shall also 
notify, as additional information to this Prospectus, the CNMV, the governing authority 
of AIAF and the Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de Registro, Compensación y 
Liquidación de Valores, S A. 
.
The Nominal Interest Rate determined for Notes of each Class for the subsequent 
Interest Accrual Periods shall be informed to the Noteholders as provided in 
paragraphs III.5.3 a) and c). 
For the purposes of the issue of the Notes and during their life, “Business Days” 
shall mean any day other than: 
¾ 
a Saturday, 
¾ 
a Sunday, 
¾ 
a day on which the Trans European Automated Real-Time Gross Settlement 
Express Transfer System (the TARGET System) in force is closed for 
business, which in 2005 are: January 1, Good Friday, Easter Monday, May 1, 
December 25 and December 26, 
¾ 
a day which is a public holiday in Madrid.

II.10.3. Dates, place, entities and procedure for payment of interest 
The interest accrued by the all Classes of Notes will be paid on January 15, April 15, 
July 15 and October 15 of each year, the first Payment Date being October 17, 2005, 
until the Notes are fully repaid (each one of these dates subject as provided below, a 
"Payment Date") in accordance with the procedure set out in paragraph II.12 of the 
Prospectus.  
In the case that any of the dates set forth in the above paragraph are not Business 
Days, the Payment Date will be the next subsequent Business Day, with interest 
corresponding to the current Interest Accrual Period described in paragraph II.10.1.a), 
accruing up to the above mentioned next subsequent Business Date, not inclusive. 
The first Payment Date of interest for all Classes of Notes will be October 17, 2005, 
with interest accruing at the relevant Nominal Interest Rate from the Disbursement 
Date (provided in paragraph II.18.5), inclusive, up until but not including October 17, 
2005. 
Interest to be paid on each Payment Date for each Interest Accrual Period will be 
calculated in accordance with the following formula: 
I = P x R x d/360 
Being: 
 
I = Interest to be paid on a given Payment Date 
 
P = Unpaid Principal Balance of each Note on the Calculation Date 
corresponding to such Payment Date 
 
R = Nominal Interest Rate expressed in annual percentage 
 
d = Number of effective days which correspond to each Interest Accrual 
Period 
 
 
45 


 
Interest accrued in favour of the Noteholders of all Classes of Notes, calculated as 
provided above, and the amount of the accrued but unpaid interest, shall be 
communicated as described in paragraph III.5.3.a) of the Prospectus, at least one (1) 
calendar day in advance of each Payment Date. 
The payment of the accrued interest of the Notes shall take place on each Payment 
Date, provided that the Fund has sufficient liquidity for such purpose in accordance 
with the payment priority order provided in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 of the Prospectus and 
the exceptional rules set forth in paragraph V.5.2. and the payment priority order in 
the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph V.6.1. and the exceptional 
rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
In the event that the Fund fails to provide for the total or partial payment of interest 
accrued on the Notes of either Class on a given Payment Date in accordance with the 
relevant payment priority order set forth in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 of the Prospectus and 
the exceptional rules set forth in paragraph V.5.2 and the payment priority order in 
the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph V.6.1. and the exceptional 
rules established in paragraph V.6.2., the amounts which the Noteholders have not 
received shall be paid on the next Payment Date. Any deferred amounts of interest 
will accrue, in favour of the Noteholders, at the same interest rate as that applied to 
the Unpaid Principal Balance of the Notes of their respective Class during the Interest 
Accrual Period/s until the Payment Date on which such deferred amounts of interest 
are paid, without accruing any interest for delayed payment and not involving any 
capitalisation of the debt. 
The Fund may not defer payment of interest of the Notes to a date later than January 
15, 2038 or, if this is a non-Business Day, the next Business Day (hereinafter, the 
“Final Maturity Date”). 
The financial servicing of the Notes will be carried out by the Financial Agent, who has 
entered into the Financial Services Agreement with the Managing Company, on behalf 
of the Fund. 
In order to better explain to the subscriber the calculation system used for fixing the 
applicable Nominal Interest Rate and the amount of interest which may correspond to 
each Note on each Payment Date, paragraph II.12 shows a practical example as well 
as theoretical charts in relation to the financial servicing of the loan. 
II.11. 
Repayment of securities 
II.11.1. Repayment price specifying the existence of any premiums, lots or any 
other financial benefits 
The repayment price for all Classes of Notes will be one hundred thousand (100,000) 
euros per Note, equivalent to 100% of their nominal amount, to be paid in 
instalments on each Payment Date. 
 
 
46 


 
All the Notes in the same Class will be repaid in equal amounts by reducing the 
nominal amount of each one of them. The amount to be reimbursed for the 
repayment of the Notes of each Class on each Payment Date will be determined in 
accordance with provisions set forth in paragraph II.11.3. 
II.11.2. Brief reference to the ordinal number of the payments of principal of the 
securities issued by the Fund in the payment priority order of the said Fund, 
and an accurate indication of the paragraph of this Prospectus where the 
rules of order of priority established for the payments of the Fund may be 
found, in particular those which affect the payment of principal of such 
securities

the payment priority order in the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in 
paragraph V.6.1. and the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
The payment of the principal of the Class A2 Notes occupies ninth (9th) place in the 
payment priority order established in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules 
set out in paragraph V.5.2 and, in particular, in accordance with the rules under 
“Allocation of the Available Principal Funds for Repayment between the Notes of each 
of the Classes” that are established in paragraph II.11.3.2.1. and sixth (6th) place in 
the payment priority order in the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in 
paragraph V.6.1. and the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
The payment of the principal of the Class B Notes occupies tenth (10th) place in the

set out in paragraph V.5.2 and, in particular, in accordance with the rules under

The payment of the principal of the Class C Notes occupies eleventh (11th) place in

set out in paragraph V.5.2 and, in particular, in accordance with the rules under
