II.11.3. Modes of repayment, specifying their dates, place, entities, procedure and 
publicity 
II.11.3.1. Final Repayment 
The Final Maturity Date and date of final repayment for all Classes of Notes will be 
January 15, 2038 or, in the event this date is not a Business Day, the next Business 
Day, without prejudice to any early repayment of the Notes that the Managing 
Company may carry out in the name and on behalf of the Fund in accordance with 
paragraph II.11.3.3 below. In which case, the Payment Date when such early 
repayment takes place will be the final date of repayment of the Notes. 
II.11.3.2. Partial repayment 
Notwithstanding the aforesaid, the Fund will make, through its Managing Company, 
partial repayments of all Classes of Notes in the terms which are described below. 
1. 
Repayment dates  
The repayment dates will coincide with the Payment Dates for interest and 
accordingly will be January 15, April 15, July 15 and October 15 of each year or, if 
applicable, the next Business Day, the first Payment Date being October 17, 2005, in 
accordance all as determined under paragraph II.10.3, up until their full repayment. 
Class A1 Notes 
The repayment of the Class A1 Notes will be carried out pro rata between them on 
each Payment Date, by reducing the nominal value of each Note until repayment is 
completed. 
The first Payment Date of the Class A1 Notes will be October 17, 2005, in accordance 
with the rules set forth in paragraph II.10.3. 
Class A2 Notes 
The repayment of the Class A2 Notes will be carried out pro rata between them on 
each Payment Date, by reducing the nominal value of each Note until repayment is 
completed. 
The first Payment Date of the Class A2 Notes will be the Payment Date on which Class 
A1 Notes are fully repaid.  
 
 
48 


 
Class B Notes 
The repayment of the Class B Notes will be carried out pro rata between them on 
each Payment Date, as the case may be, by reducing the nominal value of each Note 
until repayment is completed. 
Class C Notes 
The repayment of the Class C Notes will be carried out pro rata between them on 
each Payment Date, as the case may be, by reducing the nominal value of each Note 
until repayment is completed. 
Class D Notes 
The repayment of the Class D Notes will be carried out pro rata between them on 
each Payment Date, as the case may be, by reducing the nominal value of each Note 
until repayment is completed. 
Even if the Class A2 Notes have not been fully repaid, Class B Notes,  Class C Notes 
and Class D Notes may be partially repaid in accordance with the following rules of 
“Allocation of the Available Principal Funds for Repayment between the Notes of each 
of the Classes”: 
1st Available Principal Funds for Repayment shall be fully allocated for repayment of 
Class A1 Notes until the Payment Date on which Class A1 Notes have been fully 
repaid. 
2nd Once Class A1 Notes have been fully repaid and until the first Payment Date 
(included) on which the Unpaid Principal Balance of Class B, Class C and Class D 
Notes is, in comparison with the Unpaid Principal Balance of all Classes of Notes, 
equal or greater than 6.3%, the Available Principal Funds for Repayment shall be fully 
allocated for repayment of Class A2 Notes.  
3rd After the Payment Date on which the ratio between the Unpaid Principal Balance 
of Class B, Class C and Class D Notes and the Unpaid Principal Balance of all Classes 
of Notes, is equal or greater than 6.3%, the Available Principal Funds for Repayment 
shall be allocated for repayment of Class A2, B, C and D Notes, pro rata among them, 
in such a way that the ratio remains at 6.3% or the nearest higher percentage. 
This notwithstanding, pro rata repayment of Class A2, B, C and D Notes shall be 
interrupted and the Available Principal Funds for Repayment shall be allocated for 
repayment of the Classes on a sequential basis in accordance with their priority order 
on any Payment Date on which any of the following circumstances occurs: 
a) 
The Principal Balance of the Mortgage Shares with a delay in payment of overdue 
amounts greater than ninety (90) days is higher than 2% of the Principal Balance of 
 
 
49 


 
the Mortgage Shares on the Calculation Date corresponding to the current Payment 
Date. 
b) 
The amount of the Reserve Fund is lower than its Required Amount. 
Once the circumstances producing the interruption in the pro rata repayment of 
Classes A2, B, C and D have disappeared, the referred pro rata repayment will be 
carried out again.  
4th After the first Payment Date on which the amount of the Mortgage Shares 
pending repayment is lower than 10% of their initial amount, pro rata repayment of 
Classes A2, B, C and D Notes shall be interrupted and the Available Principal Funds for 
Repayment shall be allocated for repayment of the Classes on a sequential basis in 
accordance with their priority order until their repayment is completed. 
Any amounts that the Noteholders may not collect as a result of the existence of a 
Principal Deficiency will be paid on the next Payment Date on which it may be 
possible, such amounts providing no right to any additional or delayed payment 
interest whatsoever (since they will form part of the affected Unpaid Principal Balance 
of the Notes of the same Class on which the calculation of the payment of interest will 
be based as provided in paragraph II.10.3 above). 
The Managing Company will notify to the Noteholders as provided in paragraph 
III.5.3.a) the repayment amounts to be distributed, the Unpaid Principal Balances of 
the Notes, the Principal Deficiency, if any, as well as the actual rates of early 
repayment of the Participated Mortgage Loans and their remaining term estimated on 
the Calculation Date previous to each Payment Date. 
2. 
Calculation Dates and Periods   
"Calculation Dates" are those in which the Managing Company on behalf of the 
Fund, will carry out the required calculations to distribute or withhold the Funds 
Available on such dates, in accordance with the payment priority order set forth in 
paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules set out in paragraph V.5.2. and the 
payment priority order in the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph 
V.6.1. and the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
The Calculation Date for each relevant period will be the fifth (5th) Business Day prior 
to each Payment Date and the periods comprised between two subsequent 
Calculation Dates will be called "Calculation Periods", with the initial Calculation 
Date being included in each Calculation Period and the final Calculation Date being 
excluded. 
As an exception, the first Calculation Period will be that comprised between the 
Incorporation Date (inclusive) and the first Calculation Date (exclusive). 
3. 
Unpaid Principal Balances of the Notes 
 
 
50 


 
“Unpaid Principal Balances of the Notes” will be the balances of the principal of 
the Notes pending amortisation, including the amounts of principal accrued on 
previous Payment Dates and not paid due to lack of Available Funds, as provided in 
paragraph 4 below, and in accordance with the payment priority order described in 
paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules set out in paragraph V.5.2. and the 
payment priority order in the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph 
V.6.1. and the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
4. 
Principal Due for Repayment on each Payment Date 
The “Principal Due for Repayment” of all Classes of Notes, without distinguishing 
between them, will be equal to the difference between the Unpaid Principal Balance of 
the Notes and the Principal Balance of the Mortgage Shares, in accordance with the 
following paragraph, on the Calculation Date prior to each Payment Date, provided 
that such difference is positive. 
The “Principal Balance of the Mortgage Shares” will, for these purposes, be the 
sum of (i) the capital outstanding and (ii) the capital due but not paid to the Fund, on 
each of the Mortgage Shares, less in this latter case the capital of the Participated 
Mortgage Loans, whether due or not, with a delay in the payment of any principal or 
interest overdue amounts equal to or greater than eighteen (18) months. 
With the purpose of illustrating this concept, let us imagine the following practical 
case:

•

20,000,000 
 
 
 
In this illustration, the Principal Due for Repayment of the Notes will be twenty million 
(20,000,000) euros.

8, 10, and 12 in accordance with the payment priority order in the event of liquidation 
of the Fund set forth in paragraph V.6.1., in the light of the exceptional rules set out 
in paragraph V.6.2. 
 
The “Principal Deficiency” will be the positive difference, if any, between the 
Principal Due for Repayment of the Notes and the Available Principal Funds for 
Repayment on any given date.

II.11.3.3.  Early Repayment 
Without prejudice to the obligation of the Fund, through the Managing Company, to 
repay the Notes on the Final Maturity Date or partially on each Payment Date, the 
Managing Company will be empowered, subject to prior communication to the CNMV, 
to liquidate the Fund on a Payment Date, if the amount of Mortgage Shares pending 
repayment is less than 10% of the initial balance of the Mortgage Shares portfolio in 
accordance with Article 5.3 of Law 19/1992. This faculty will be subject to the 
condition that the early repayment of the Mortgage Shares plus the existing balance 
of the Cash Account and, if appropriate, of the Excess Balance Account, allows a total 
cancellation of the obligations due to the Noteholders (in the manner established in 
paragraph III.8.1), after fulfilling the payment priority order as described in paragraph 
V.6.1 and the exceptional rules set out in paragraph V.6.2. 
Article 5.6 of Law 19/1992 requires that the flows of principal and interests 
corresponding to the Notes issued by the Fund coincide with the cash flows generated 
by the Mortgage Shares contained in the Fund, without any temporary lags other than 
those which derive from the fees and the administrative and management expenses, 
insurance premiums or other applicable items. If by reason of any event or 
exceptional circumstance not expected on the date the Incorporation Deed was 
 
 
52 


 
executed, the financial balance of the Fund required by Law 19/1992 is permanently 
and negatively affected for reasons not attributable to the operation of the Fund, such 
as a new legal regime or additional legal regulations, withholdings or other situations 
that could affect this balance permanently, the Managing Company may be entitled to 
repay the Notes in advance, in the name and on behalf of the Fund. For the avoidance 
of doubt, the possible existence of a Principal Deficiency shall not in itself be 
considered as causing a deterioration of the financial balance of the Fund to the 
extent this arises in the ordinary course of the Fund’s business. 
The Managing Company, in the name and on behalf of the Fund, may also early 
liquidate the Fund in the event that: (i) the Mortgage Shares are fully repaid, (ii) a 
relevant breach of payment exists or it is foreseen that there will be one, and such 
breach produces a significant permanent unbalance related to any of the Notes 
issued, or (iii) the Notes are fully repaid (no later than the Final Maturity Date).  
In addition, the early liquidation of the Fund and the repayment of the Notes will take 
place in the event that the Managing Company is declared to be in liquidation or 
insolvency (“concurso”) in case its authorisation has been revoked and a new 
Managing Company has not been designated within a term of four months in 
accordance with paragraph III.3.1. 
The early repayment as a consequence of the occurrence of the above events will be 
implemented as per the terms and conditions established in paragraph III.8.1.

a) 
Practical example of the calculation of the Nominal Interest rate 
In accordance with paragraph II.10.3 and in order to make it easier for the 
Noteholder to understand the calculation system used for the Nominal Interest Rate 
and the amount of interest to be received per Class A1 Note on each Payment Date, 
the example given below shows the calculation for this Class.  
¾ 
3 month Euribor Rate: 2.126% 
¾ 
Spread: 0.05% 
¾ 
Amount of interest per Note:  
 
 
 
53 


 
Period of interest for each Note:  
 
90 days 
Unpaid Principal Balance of the Note:   
100,000 Euros 
Calculation of accrued interest per Note: 
100,000 x 2.176% x 90/360 = 544 euros 
The amount of interest to be received for each Class A1 Note would be 546.5 Euros 
on an Unpaid Balance of Principal of the Note of 100,000 Euros. The example would 
be identical for the Class B, C and D Notes, substituting the spread of 0.05% of the 
Class A1 Notes in the example, by the spread of the relevant Class. 
With respect to the first Interest Accrual Period, an example of the calculation of the 
reference interest rate resulting from the interpolation follows: 
¾ 
4 month Euribor:  2.135% 
 
120 days 
¾ 
5 month Euribor:  2.141% 
 
150 days 
150 - 120 = 30 days 
2.141% - 2.135% = 0.006% 
If we divide 0.006% by 30: = 0.0002% 
If we want to calculate the reference interest rate for 125 days (from June 14, 2005 
(Disbursement Date), included, to October 17, 2005 (first Payment Date), excluded): 
(125 - 120) x 0.0002% = 0.001% 
Finally: 
2.135% + 0.001% = 2.136% 
Note that in this example the resulting percentage has been added from the 4 month 
Euribor because the slope of the curve is positive (that is, the 4 month Euribor is 
lower than the 5 month Euribor). 
Once the reference interest rate resulting from the interpolation has been fixed, the 
amount of interest to be received shall be calculated as described above for any 
Interest Accrual Period. 
b) 
Table of the financial service of the loan 
The main characteristic of mortgage securitisation bonds is their periodic repayment. 
As a result, their average life and duration depend fundamentally on the speed at 
which mortgagors repay their loans. 
The anticipated repayments that the debtors decide to make, subject to continuing 
changes and estimated in the Prospectus through the use of the constant annual rate 
 
 
54 


 
of early repayment or future prepayment (hereinafter, "CPR"), will affect the speed of 
repayment of the Participated Mortgage Loans and the average life and duration of 
the Notes directly. 
Other variables exist and are also subject to continuing changes, which affect the 
average life and duration of the Notes. The variables and their hypothetical values 
assumed in all the charts provided in this section are the following: 
¾ 
interest rate of the Mortgage Shares portfolio: 2.743 (average nominal interest rate 
weighted at May 16, 2005);   
¾ 
proportion of the Mortgage Shares portfolio in arrears: 0%;   
¾ 
proportion of the Mortgage Shares portfolio in default: 0%;   
¾ 
rate of early repayment: constant throughout the lifetime of the Notes;   
¾ 
Disbursement Date of the Notes: June 14, 2005; 
¾ 
Amount of Principal Deficiency: none. 
The actual adjusted duration of the Notes shall also depend on their floating interest 
rates, and on all the charts provided in this section the rate is assumed as constant at  
2.176% for the Class A1 Notes, 2.276% for the Class A2 Notes, 2.386% the Class B 
Notes, 2.626% for the Class C Notes and 3.876% for the Class D Notes, except for 
the first Interest Accrual Period, in which the sum of the reference interest rate 
resulting from the interpolation and the relevant spread of each Class results in a rate 
of 2.186% for Class A1 Notes, 2.286 for Class A2 Notes, 2.396% for Class B Notes, 
2.636% for Class C Notes and 3.886% for Class D Notes.

II.15. 
Existence or non-existence of special guarantees of the Mortgage Shares 
that are grouped together in the Fund or of the securities issued by the 
Fund, which could have been granted by some of the entities involved in the 
securitisation process described by the Prospectus 
There are no special guarantees given in respect of the Mortgage Shares or the Notes, 
except the following undertakings that the Issuer assumes while the Mortgage Shares 
are in force: 
(1) 
to substitute each and all Mortgage Shares derived from Participated 
Mortgage Loans which did not conform, as of the Incorporation Date, to the 
statements contained in paragraph IV.1.a), with other Mortgage Shares with 
homogeneous characteristics of maturity, interest rate, unpaid capital balance and 
credit quality which may be grouped together in a Mortgage Securitisation Fund, in 
accordance with paragraph IV.1.d). If it is not possible, the Issuer undertakes to 
repay the affected Mortgage Shares, reimbursing in cash the unpaid capital balance, 
the unpaid accrued interest, as well as any amount that could be due to the Fund until 
that date, in accordance with paragraph IV.1.d); 
(2) 
likewise, without prejudice to paragraph IV.1.a), the Issuer undertakes that 
if any mortgagor has any credit claim against the Issuer and decides to exercise it by 
setting-off this credit against the debt derived from a Participated Mortgage Loan, the 
Issuer will communicate it to the Managing Company and will pay to the Fund, in the 
bank account that the Managing Company may indicate or open for this purpose, an 
amount equal to the set-off amount which would otherwise have been due to the 
Fund. 
Both (i) the amounts that the Issuer may receive from the mortgagors as principal, 
ordinary interest and arrears interest applicable to each relevant Participated 
Mortgage Loan, and (ii) all the amounts that may be paid to the Issuer as designated 
beneficiary of the insurance policies which have been subscribed by the mortgagors of 
the Participated Mortgage Loans (or any other insurance policy which may grant an 
equivalent cover) and have been assigned by the Issuer to the Fund, will be delivered 
by the Issuer to the Fund through the Managing Company. 
None of the previous undertakings of the Issuer shall be understood as a payment 
guarantee in case of default of the mortgagors.

II.17. 
Secondary organised markets for which there is an obligation to request the 
listing and specific maximum term in which such request and the other 
required documents must be submitted to obtain the listing 
In accordance with article 5.9 of Law 19/1992, immediately after the granting of the 
Incorporation Deed and once the disbursement of the Notes has been completed (as 
referred to in paragraph II.18.5), the Managing Company will request the listing of the 
Notes in the AIAF Fixed-Interest Securities Market. It is expected that actual listing 
will take place no later than thirty (30) days following the Disbursement Date (as 
defined in paragraph II.18.5). 
The Managing Company expressly acknowledges that it is aware of the requirements 
and conditions required for listing, permanence and delisting of securities from AIAF in 
accordance with the legislation currently in force and the requirements of its 
governing bodies, and the Fund agrees, through the Managing Company, to fulfil and 
comply with them. 
In the event that the listing of the Notes in the AIAF is not completed within the 
above period, the Managing Company will immediately inform the Noteholders and 
will specify the reasons, by means of an announcement published in a newspaper that 
is distributed nation-wide, in accordance with the provisions of paragraph III.5.3.b) 
and c).  Such actions shall be without prejudice to the contractual liability of the 
Managing Company that could result from the listing of the Notes in the AIAF not 
being completed within the above period. 
II.18. 
Applications for subscription or acquisition 
II.18.1. Group of potential investors to whom the securities are offered, stating the 
reasons for choosing them 
It is intended that the Notes will be on-sold to institutional or qualified investors. For 
this purpose, institutional or qualified investors shall be those mentioned in Article 7.1, 
paragraph a) of Royal Decree 291/1992 of March 27, on issues and public offerings 
for the sale of securities, as amended by Royal Decree 2590/1998, of December 7, 
and others described in EU Directive 2003/71/CE. 
II.18.2. Legal suitability of the Notes 
The following legal considerations are applicable to the Notes, for the purposes of 
being subscribed by certain investors: 
(i) 
In accordance with the Ministerial Order of December 30, 1992, on solvency 
regulations of Credit Entities and the Ministerial Order of December 29, 1992, on 
equity and supervision on a consolidated base of securities companies and agencies 
and their groups, as modified both by Ministerial Order of April 13, 2000 and, among 
others, by the Order of December 27, 2002, the former, and the Order of January 8, 
2003, the latter, securities issued by Mortgage Securitisation Funds set out in Law 
19/1992 have a weighting of 50% regarding the solvency ratio which these entities 
 
 
66 


 
 
 
t
should maintain, provided that their credit quality, in the opinion of CNMV, is at least, 
the same as that of the underlying mortgage credits. 
The CNMV, on the date of registration of the Prospectus, has granted the weighting 
value mentioned in the preceding paragraph to the Class A1 and Class A2 Notes, as a 
result of the following factors: (i) that the Participated Mortgage Loans have been 
granted with first mortgage guarantee over residential property located in Spain; (ii) 
that the Participated Mortgage Loans and the Mortgage Shares comply with the 
requirements of the regulations in force in the mortgage market; (iii) that the principal 
of each of the Participated Mortgage Loans does not exceed 80% of the appraisal 
value of the corresponding property mortgaged in guarantee; (iv) that the statements 
made by the Issuer provided in the Chapter IV are correct; and (v) that the ratings 
granted by the Rating Agencies, as an assessment of the financial risk of the Notes 
are as provided in paragraph II.3. 
The Class B, the Class C and the Class D Notes do not have the 50% weighting value 
for the solvency ratio of Credit Entities and securities companies and agencies referred 
to in the above mentioned regulations. 
(ii) 
The Notes are eligible for investment by Insurance Entities and their 
technical provisions, in accordance with Article 50.5 of the Regulation on Ordination 
and Supervision of the Private Insurance, approved by Royal Decree 2486/1998, of 
November 20, as amended by Royal Decree 297/2004, of February 20, among others. 
(iii) 
The Notes are eligible for investment by the Technical Provisions Fund of the
Sociedades de Garantía Recíproca, in accordance with Law 1/1994, of March 11, on 
the Legal Regime of the Sociedades de Garan ía Recíproca, and Royal Decree 
2345/1996, of November 8, on administrative authorisation rules and requirements of 
solvency for Sociedades de Garantía Recíproca. 
(iv) 
The Notes are eligible for investment by Pension Funds in accordance with 
Article 70 of Royal Decree 304/2004, of February 20, approving the Regulation of 
Pension Plans and Funds. 
(v) 
The Notes are eligible for investment by Collective Investment Institutions in 
accordance with the common rules established in Article 23 and with the particular 
rules established for each one of them in Articles 30 (Financial Collective Investment 
Institutions) and 36 (Real Estate Collective Investment Institutions) of Law 35/2003, 
of November 4, on Collective Investment Institutions and, until its subsequent 
regulations come into force and provided that they do not oppose the said Law, in 
accordance with Royal Decree 1393/1990, of November 2, as amended by Royal 
Decree 91/2001, of February 2, among others, and with the Order of May 28, 1999 
which partially amends the Order of June 7, 1990, on Collaboration Agreements 
regarding Investment Funds on Government Stock). 
II.18.3. Date or Period of subscription or acquisition 
 
67 


 
The subscription period (the “Subscription Period”) will have a duration of five (5) 
hours from 13:00 to 18:00 hours of the first Business Day following the Incorporation 
Date (i.e. June 10, 2005). 
II.18.4. Where and before whom may the subscription or acquisition be processed? 
The applications for subscription must be carried out through any means permitted by 
law, during the Subscription Period, addressed to Barclays Bank PLC, acting through 
its investment banking division Barclays Capital, Caja de Ahorros de Valencia, 
Castellón y Alicante (”Bancaja”) and Caja de Ahorros y Monte de Piedad de Madrid 
(“Caja Madrid”) in their capacity as underwriting entities of the Notes issue 
(hereinafter and for these purposes, the “Underwriting Entities”). Likewise, in the 
event that, in accordance with paragraph II.19.1 below, Barclays Bank, S.A. assumes 
the underwriting commitments of those Underwriting Entities which do not accept the 
final spreads determined by the Managing Company or who have invoked any of the 
conditions for termination of the Underwriting Agreement established therein, the 
applications for subscription may be also addressed to Barclays Bank, S.A. The 
Underwriting Entities whose underwriting commitments are terminated may not 
receive applications for subscription, which shall only be carried out through the 
remaining Underwriting Entities or Barclays Bank, S.A., as the case may be. 
In the event that the Entidad Directora and the Underwriting Entities do not reach an 
agreement on the final spreads applicable to the Classes of Notes before 9:00 hours 
of the day of commencement of the Subscription Period or in the event that the 
Underwriting Agreement is terminated due to the Underwriting Entities invoking any 
of the conditions established therein before 10:00 hours of the Disbursement Date 
(vid. paragraph II.19.1), the Managing Company shall determine the final spreads on 
its own and shall communicate to the CNMV that Barclays Bank, S.A. will finally act as 
Underwriting Entity by virtue of its underwriting commitment referred to in paragraphs 
II.19.1 and V.4.2 of the Prospectus and established in the underwriting agreement 
subject to the said conditions precedent. 
II.18.5. Method and dates for disbursement 
The investors to whom the Notes have been sold shall pay to the Underwriting 
Entities, before 10.00 hours in Madrid on the second Business Day following the 
closing date of the Subscription Period (i.e. June 14, 2005) (the “Disbursement 
Date”), for same-day value, the price of issue (100% of the nominal amount) which 
may correspond to each Note assigned to them in the subscription. 
Once Barclays Bank, S.A. is notified by fax (fax no. +34913361429), each 
Underwriting Entity shall pay the aggregate committed amount of the Notes assigned 
to them, less their underwriting fee, to the account opened by Barclays Bank, S.A. at 
the Bank of Spain (account no. 01 01 40 06 50 and code BARCESMM), which in its 
capacity as Financial Agent shall pay to the Fund, at the Cash Account, on the same 
date, all funds received from the Underwriting Entities, after deducting the 
 
 
68 


 
arrangement fee, before 12:00 hours a.m. in Madrid, for same-day value, in 
accordance with the provisions of the Underwriting Agreement. 
II.18.6. Method and term of delivery to subscribers of the copies of the subscription

any, and their maximum validity period 
No later than five (5) days from the Disbursement Date, each investor will receive 
from the Underwriting Entity through which it has subscribed the Notes, a document

disbursed for such subscription. 
Such supporting document will not be negotiable and will be valid to prove the 
subscription of the relevant Notes until their registration in the accounting record as 
provided in paragraph II.5.

Spanish law. 
II.22. 
Taxation of income derived from the Notes 
The following is a summary of the tax regime applicable to the investments derived 
from the offer. This summary is based on laws which are currently in force in Spain.  
 
73 


 
Investors must take into account both their particular tax circumstances and the rules 
of territorial application and the legislation in force at the time the income is obtained. 
Since the Notes are registered in book-entry form and a request will be made for their 
listing in a Spanish official secondary market, and considering that such circumstances 
are significant when determining the taxes to be paid, it has been assumed that both 
conditions will be complied with. Likewise, it has been considered that the Notes will 
be regarded, at the time of their issuance, as financial assets with an explicit return 
whenever such circumstance may prove significant for taxation purposes. 
Any withholdings, payments on account and taxes already established or which may 
be established in the future on the principal, interest or earnings of the Notes will be 
borne by their holders and their amount will be deducted by the Managing Company, 
if applicable, following the procedures established by law. 
Throughout the life of the Notes, the Fund will be subject to tax in accordance with 
the legislation currently in force at the time. 
This summary does not address all the tax considerations that may be relevant to all 
categories of potential investors, some of whom (such as financial institutions, collective 
investment institutions or “look-through” entities) may be subject to special rules.  
II.22.1. Spanish resident investors 
a) 
Individual Income Tax 
Interest and income arising from the transfer, reimbursement or redemption of the 
Notes obtained by Noteholders who may be regarded as taxpayers under the 
Individual Income Tax (IIT), will be deemed income from movable property in 
accordance with the terms provided for in Article 23.2 of Royal Legislative Decree 
3/2004 of March 5 on Individual Income Tax. 
In this regard, income derived from the coupon payments will be equal to the gross 
amount of the coupon, including the amount withheld, if any, in accordance with the 
IIT Regulations. 
In the event of transfer, reimbursement or redemption of the Notes, income will be 
equal to the difference between their transfer, reimbursement or redemption value 
(deducting the additional expenses incurred in the transfer, provided they are duly 
justified) and their acquisition or subscription value (adding the additional expenses 
incurred in the acquisition, provided they are duly justified). 
Losses derived from the transfer of the Notes, when the taxpayer had acquired other 
Notes within the two months prior or subsequent to such transfer, shall be included in 
its taxable base when the remaining Notes are transferred. 
The resulting net taxable income shall be determined by deducting the management 
and deposit expenses from the gross income, excluding those pertaining to 
discretionary and individualized portfolio management. If the income was generated 
 
 
74 


 
after a two-year holding period, the individual taxpayer will benefit from a 40% 
reduction on the taxable income. 
Interest received by the Noteholders will be subject to a withholding tax on account of 
the investor’s final IIT liability (currently, at a 15% rate), in accordance with the 
provisions set forth in Royal Decree 1775/2004 of July 30, on IIT Regulations.  
On the contrary, income arising on the transfer or reimbursement of the Notes will not 
be subject to withholding tax at source, given that the Notes (i) will be registered in 
book-entry form and (ii) listed in a Spanish official secondary market. 
Notwithstanding the above, a withholding tax will be applied on the part of the price 
corresponding to the accrued interest (currently, at a 15% rate) when the transfer of 
the Notes takes place within the thirty (30) days period prior to the moment in which 
such interest is due, provided that (i) the acquiror is a person or entity that is not 
resident in Spain for tax purposes or is a taxpayer under the Corporate Income Tax 
Law, and (ii) the acquiror is not subject to withholding tax at source on interest 
arising from the acquired Notes. 
b) 
Corporate Income Tax 
Interest and income arising on the transfer, redemption or reimbursement of the 
Notes, obtained by entities that are resident in Spain for tax purposes will be taxed 
under the rules contained in Section IV of Royal Legislative Decree 4/2004 of March 5 
on Corporate Income Tax (CIT). 
Said income will not be subject to any withholding tax at source due to the fact that 
the Notes (i) will be registered in book-entry form and (ii) listed in a Spanish official 
secondary market. 
Pursuant to article 59.q) of Royal Decree 1777/2004 of July 30, said income will not 
be subject to any withholding tax at source provided that the Notes (i) will be 
registered in book-entry form and (ii) listed in a Spanish official secondary market. 
In this regard, pursuant to Order of December 22, 1999, the procedure to apply such 
withholding tax exemption with regard to interest paid to taxpayers shall be carried 
out as follows: 
1. The Managing Company, in the name and on behalf of the Fund as issuer, shall pay 
to the depositary entities, through the Financial Agent, the net amount resulting 
from the application of the general withholding rate in force (currently, 15%) to the 
gross amount of interest. 
 
2. Before the 10th day following the end of the month following that month in which 
each interest coupon was due, the depositary entities shall submit to the Managing 
Company or the Financial Agent a list of CIT taxpayers including their identity, the 
 
 
75 


 
ISIN code of the Notes, the number of Notes owned by each investor on the 
maturity date of each coupon, the gross income obtained and the amount withheld. 
 
3. The Noteholders, CIT taxpayers, shall provide evidence of ownership of the Notes to 
the depositary entities before the 10th day following the end of the month in which 
the interest coupon was due, so that the depositary entities may produce the list 
referred to in paragraph 2 above. 
 
4. As soon as it receives the referred list, the Managing Company shall immediately 
pay, through the Financial Agent, to the depositary entities the amount withheld 
from those investors that are CIT taxpayers. 
 
5. The depositary entities shall immediately pay the amount withheld to those 
Noteholders regarded as CIT taxpayers. 
In order to evidence their status as CIT taxpayers, the Noteholders may use any 
means of proof available under the law. In this regard, documents provided as 
evidence must be in possession of the depositary entity of the Notes and at the 
Issuer's disposal (the Managing Company representing the Fund) for verification 
purposes. The State Treasury must also be allowed access to this information. A 
photocopy of the Tax Identification Number will be sufficient for this purpose. 
II.22.2. Non-Spanish resident investors 
Interest and other income arising from the transfer, reimbursement or redemption of 
the Notes obtained by Noteholders that are not resident in Spain for tax purposes, 
either through a permanent establishment located in Spain or otherwise, will be 
considered Spanish sourced income and, therefore, subject to taxation in Spain under 
the terms of Article 12 of Royal Legislative Decree 5/2004 of March 5, on Non-
Residents Income Tax (NRIT). 
a) 
Income obtained through a permanent establishment located in Spain 
Income deriving from the Notes obtained through a permanent establishment in Spain 
will be taxed in accordance with the rules provided by Chapter III of the 
aforementioned Royal Legislative Decree 5/2004, of March 5, notwithstanding the 
applicable Conventions for the avoidance of  Double Taxation entered into by Spain. 
The withholding rules applicable to CIT taxpayers will be applicable to NRIT taxpayers 
who obtain income through a permanent establishment in Spain. 
Thus, such income will not be subject to withholding tax at source given that the 
Notes will be registered in book-entry form and listed in a Spanish official secondary 
market. 
The procedure to apply this withholding tax exemption with respect to interest 
payments is established by the Order of December 22, 1999. 
 
 
76 


 
b) 
Income not obtained through a permanent establishment located in Spain 
Interest as well as income arising from the transfer, reimbursement or redemption of 
the Notes obtained by individuals and entities non-resident in Spain for tax purposes 
and not acting in Spain with respect to the Notes through a permanent establishment 
located in Spain will be subject to tax in accordance with the rules set forth in Chapter 
IV of the aforementioned Royal Legislative Decree 5/2005, of March 5. The following 
is a summary of these rules, without prejudice to the provisions established by the 
Conventions for the avoidance of  Double Taxation (CDT) entered into by Spain that 
may determine exemption from the relevant income or, as the case may be, 
application of reduced tax rates: 
¾ The taxable base will be equal to the gross amount obtained, calculated in 
accordance with the rules set forth in Individual Income Tax Law, without applying 
the reductions provided under the said Law. 
¾ In the event of transfer, reimbursement or redemption of the Notes, the taxable 
income will be calculated taking into account the additional expenses incurred in the 
acquisition and transfer of such Notes, provided that they are appropriately 
evidenced. Taxpayers will be taxed separately for each total or partial accrual of 
income subject to taxation, without the possibility of setting off such accruals 
against each other. 
¾ Income obtained from the Notes by individuals or entities non-resident in Spain and 
that do not act through a permanent establishment located in Spain will be exempt 
from taxation in Spain when obtained by residents in another EU Member State or 
by a permanent establishment of the said residents in another EU Member State, 
provided that the relevant certificate of residence issued by the tax authorities of the 
country in which the investor resides is furnished. Said certificate will be valid for a 
term of one year from the date of issuance. 
¾ Likewise, income deriving from the transfer of these securities in a Spanish official 
secondary market will be exempt, if obtained by individuals or entities that are 
residents of a State that has entered into a CDT with Spain that includes an 
exchange of information. For this purpose, a certificate of tax residence issued by 
the tax authorities of the country in which the investor resides must be furnished 
(expressly stating that the investor is resident within the meaning of the relevant 
CDT), or, where appropriate, a specific form provided in the Order Regulation which 
further regulates the relevant CDT. Said certificate will be valid for a term of one 
year from the date of issuance. 
¾ The exemptions described in the preceding paragraphs shall in no event be 
applicable when the income is obtained through countries or territories regarded as 
tax havens, as provided in Royal Decree 1080/1991, of July 5. 
 
 
77 


 
¾ The tax quota will be calculated by applying the tax rate of 15% to the above 
taxable base, unless an internal exemption or a reduced tax rate provided by a CDT 
is applicable. In the latter event, the application of the reduced tax rate established 
in the CDT will require the submission of a certificate of tax residence in the terms 
established above. Such certificate must expressly state that the investor is resident 
within the meaning of the relevant CDT. 
¾ Income obtained by the non-Spanish resident Noteholders may be subject to 
withholding on account of NRIT, according to the following rules: 
¾ The payment of interest on the Notes will be subject to withholding tax on 
account of NRIT, except for the cases where the payment of the tax or the 
applicability of an exemption is evidenced. The withholding, if applicable, will be 
equal to the final tax quota, calculated according to the rules described above. 
¾ However, no withholding tax will be due on income deriving from the transfer or 
reimbursement of the Notes, since they will be registered in book-entry form and 
listed in a Spanish official secondary market. 
¾ In such cases in which financial entities domiciled, resident or represented in 
Spain take part in the payment procedure of the interest derived from the Notes 
as depositary or collection manager of the income derived from such securities, 
the withholding procedure shall be carried out in accordance with the procedure 
established by the Order of April 13, 2000, as follows: 
1. 
The Fund shall transfer to the depositary entities, directly or through its 
Financial Agent, on each coupon payment date, the net amount resulting 
from the application of the general withholding general rate in force on such 
date (currently, 15%) to the gross amount of interest.  
2. 
The depositary entities shall submit to the Managing Company or the 
Financial Agent, before the 10th day following the end of the month in which 
the interest coupon was due, a list of the non-Spanish resident Noteholders, 
including information relating to the class and maturity date of the Notes, 
identification and residence of the Noteholders, the number of Notes held by 
each investor on the maturity date of each coupon, the relevant gross 
income obtained and the amount to be withheld.  
3. 
Non-Spanish residents shall, on their part, have evidenced before the 
depositary entities their residence for tax purposes by means of a certificate 
of residence issued by the tax authorities of their country of residence, 
where it must be expressly stated, in the event that a withholding exemption 
or a reduced tax rate applies in accordance with a CDT, that such investor is 
resident in such country within the meaning of the relevant CDT. This 
certificate is valid for a period of one (1) year as of the date of issuance. 
Nevertheless, if a reduced tax rate provided by a CDT is applicable and such 
 
 
78 


 
CDT has been developed through and Order that requires the use of a 
specific form, the tax residence shall be evidenced through the filing of such 
form. 
4. 
The Fund, as soon as it receives the list referred to in the preceding 
paragraph, shall immediately transfer, directly or through its Financial Agent, 
to the depositary entities the amount withheld from the investors who are 
entitled to apply the withholding exemption or the amount withheld in 
excess of the reduced tax rate provided by the relevant CDT. 
5. 
The depositary entities shall immediately pay to the investors on account of 
the Fund, the amount withheld or, as the case may be, the amount withheld 
in excess of the CDT reduced rate. 
In the event that the Noteholder could not properly evidence its tax residence for 
this purpose, income derived from the Notes shall be subject to the general 
taxation regime explained above. However, the affected investors may request a 
refund of the amount withheld from the Spanish Tax Authorities following the 
standard refund procedure set forth by the Spanish regulations. 
II.22.3. Indirect taxation on the subscription, acquisition and transfer of the Notes 
Subscription, acquisition and transfer of the Notes will be exempt from Transfer Tax 
and Value Added Tax. Additionally, no Stamp Duty will be levied on such transfers. 
II.22.4. Net Wealth Tax 
Spanish resident individuals who hold Notes on the last day of any year and who must  
file the corresponding return, will be subject to the general rules of the Spanish Net 
Wealth Tax on the average market value of such Notes during the last quarter of such 
year, published on an annual basis by the Spanish Ministerial Department of Economy 
and Finance. 
Non-Spanish resident individuals who hold Notes on the last day of each year will also 
be subject to the Net Wealth Tax, unless an applicable CDT entered into by Spain 
states otherwise. However, Noteholders that are resident in an EU Member State will 
be exempted with regard to the Notes whose income is exempt from NRIT in the 
terms set forth above. 
II.22.5. Inheritance and Gift Tax 
Transfers of the Notes upon death or by gift (inter vivos) in favour of individuals will be 
subject to the general rules of the Spanish Inheritance and Gift Tax, unless an 
applicable CDT states otherwise. For the cases in which the beneficiary is a corporation, 
the income obtained will be subject to CIT or NRIT, as the case may be, without 
prejudice to the provisions of the CDT that may be applicable. 
 
 
79

III.1. 
Legal background and purpose of the Fund 
 
A) Legal background and purpose of the Fund 
 
The incorporation of the Fund and the issue of the Notes are governed by Law 
19/1992, of July 7, under the Regime applicable to Companies and Funds of Real 
Estate Investment and Funds of Mortgage Securitisation. 
 
In accordance with Article 5.1 of Law 19/1992, the Fund constitutes a separate and 
closed estate, without a separate and independent legal status. As regards its assets, 
the Fund is composed of the Mortgage Shares contained in it and the Reserve Fund 
referred in paragraph V.3.4 and, as regards its liabilities, of the Notes and the 
Subordinated Loans (described in paragraphs V.3.2 and V.3.3), in such a way that the 
net value of the Fund is zero. 
 
The Mortgage Shares constituting the asset of the Fund are regulated by Law 2/1981, 
of March 25, on Regulation of the Mortgage Market and by Royal Decree 685/1982, of 
March 17, which develops certain aspects of Law 2/1981. 
 
The Fund is incorporated for the purpose of serving as vehicle to subscribe the 
Mortgage Shares issued by the Issuer, to group them together and to issue the Class 
A1, A2, B, C and D Notes. 
 
B) Issuance and subscription price of the Mortgage Shares 
The Mortgage Shares will be issued on the Incorporation Date in order to be 
subscribed by the Fund. The Mortgage Shares will be issued at value (“a la par”) and 
with a total capital value at least equal to the total amount of the Notes, that is, Euro 
700,000,000, as described in section IV.1.b). 
The Mortgage Shares refer to a participation of 100% in the principal and interest 
(including ordinary and arrears interest), of each Participated Mortgage Loan, as 
described in section IV.1.c) of this Prospectus. 
III.2. 
Complete name of the Fund and, as the case may be, abbreviated or 
commercial name set out for its identification or for the identification of its 
securities in the secondary markets 
 
The Fund will be named AyT Génova Hipotecario VI, Fondo de Titulización Hipotecaria 
and, for its identification, any of the abbreviated names listed below may be used 
interchangeably: 
¾ 
AyT Génova VI F.T.H. 
 
 
83 


 
¾ 
AyT Génova Hipotecario VI, FTH 
¾ AyT Génova VI 
¾ AyT Génova Hipotecario VI 
 
III.3. 
Management and representation of the Fund and of the holders of the 
securities issued by the Fund 
III.3.1. Description of the duties and responsibilities assumed by the Managing 
Company in the management and legal representation of the Fund and of 
the holders of the securities issued by the Fund 
 
In accordance with Article 5.2 of Law 19/1992, the management and legal 
representation of the Fund corresponds to the Managing Company, in the terms set 
out in Law 19/1992 and other applicable regulations, without prejudice to that set out 
in the Incorporation Deed. The incorporation of the Managing Company was 
authorised by the Ministry of Economy and Tax on July 16, 1993 and it is registered 
with the Special Registries of CNMV under number 5. The information on the 
Managing Company is provided in Chapter VI of this Prospectus. 
 
The resignation and substitution of the Managing Company will be governed by 
Articles 18 and 19 of Royal Decree 926/1998, of May 14, on regulation of Asset 
Securitisation Funds and on Securitisation Funds Managing Companies or by the laws 
in force at any time. The Managing Company will be entitled to request its substitution 
voluntarily, when it deems appropriate, by means of a written communication to the 
CNMV, in which the appointment of the replacement managing company will be 
included. A written communication by the new managing company of securitisation 
funds, duly authorized and registered with the Special Registries of the CNMV will also 
be attached. In this communication, the replacing managing company will declare that 
it is willing to accept such function. The resignation of the Managing Company and the 
appointment of a new managing company must be approved by the CNMV. The 
Managing Company will not be entitled to discontinue its duties until all the 
requirements and steps for the appointment of the substituting managing company 
have been completed. All the expenses that may be generated as a consequence of 
this substitution will be borne by the Managing Company and under no circumstance 
shall they be charged to the Fund. 
If the Managing Company was declared in liquidation or insolvency (“concurso”) or if 
its authorisation is revoked, it shall find a Managing Company to replace it, and the 
management and representation of the Fund will be carried out by the new managing 
company, in compliance with Articles 18 and 19 of the Royal Decree 926/1998 of May 
14 referred to. 
If after four (4) months (such period being established in Article 19.2 of the 
mentioned Royal Decree) after the event giving rise to the replacement occurred, a 
new managing company has not been appointed, an event of early termination of the 
 
 
84 


 
Fund and repayment of the Notes will exist and the actions set out in paragraph III.8 
will be carried out. 
The replacement of the Managing Company and the appointment of the new 
managing company, once approved by the CNMV, will be communicated to the Rating 
Agencies. 
The Noteholders will not take any action against the Managing Company for any 
reason other than the breach of its duties or for the non-compliance with the 
provisions of the Incorporation Deed. 
Particularly, the Managing Company, in its management duties, will carry out the 
following activities: 
(i) 
It will open, on behalf of the Fund, a bank account (hereinafter, the “Cash 
Account” referred to in paragraph V.3.1) with the Financial Agent and, as the case 
may be, the Excess Balance Account. 
The balance of this account will accrue interest at a monthly average of EONIA 
interest rate (Euro Overnight Interest Average) calculated by the European Central 
Bank and published by REUTERS in its page EONIA, corresponding to the previous 
month. This interest will be settled monthly. 
(ii) 
It will adopt the appropriate measures in order that the amounts received in 
respect of principal and interest and for any other respect that are due to the Fund, 
are deposited in the Cash Account. 
(iii) 
It will ensure that the amounts deposited in the Cash Account earn the 
profitability set forth in the Financial Services Agreement and that the amounts 
deposited, as the case may be, in the Excess Balance Account earn the profitability 
arranged for such balance.  
(iv) 
It will calculate, on each Interest Rate Fixing Date, with regard to the next 
Interest Accrual Period, the Nominal Interest Rate applicable to all Classes of Notes 
resulting from the calculation made according with paragraph II.10, and will publish it 
as set forth in paragraph III.5.3.a). 
(v) 
It will calculate, on each Calculation Date, the principal to be repaid for all 
Classes of Notes, and together with the accrued interest in accordance with paragraph 
II.11.3.2, it will publish them as set forth in paragraph III.5.3.a). 
(vi) 
It will allocate the Available Funds (referred in paragraph V.5.1.B), as well as 
any other amount available in the Cash Account and, as the case may be, in the 
Excess Balance Account, on each date, to the fulfilment of the payment or withholding 
obligations of the Fund in the terms and in the payment priority order provided for 
paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules provided in paragraph V.5.2. or in the 
 
 
85 


 
payment priority order in the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph 
V.6.1. and the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
If, at any time during the life of the Fund, the ratings of Barclays Bank PLC or its stake 
in Barclays Bank, S.A. fall below the thresholds indicated in paragraph II.4.1 above, 
Barclays Bank, S.A. will be substituted as Financial Agent by another credit entity 
whose short-term debt has a rating of at least A-1 in accordance with S&P short term 
risk scale, P-1 in accordance with Moody’s short term risk scale and F1 in accordance 
with Fitch short term risk scale (in which case, the Managing Company will transfer to 
this entity the Cash Account and will arrange for the best obtainable return of its 
balances), unless the Financial Agent (i) obtains from a credit entity with the 
mentioned minimum ratings, within thirty (30) Business Days from the assignment of 
this lower rating or from the reduction of Barclays Bank PLC’s holding in the Financial 
Agent below the above mentioned percentage, a first demand guarantee that 
guarantees to the Fund the amounts deposited in the Cash Account, or (ii) transfer 
the Cash Account of the Fund to an entity with a non-subordinated and unsecured 
short-term debt of at least A-1, P-1 and F1 ratings (in accordance with S&P, Moody’s 
and Fitch short-term debt rating scales, respectively), arranging for the best 
obtainable return of the balances of the Cash Account, or (iii) if options a) and b) 
above are not possible, the Managing Company obtains from the Financial Agent or a 
third party collateral security in favour of the Fund on financial assets with a credit 
rating of not less than that of the Spanish State Government Debt (“Deuda Pública del 
Estado Español”) in an amount sufficient to guarantee the commitments established in 
the Financial Services Agreement. In event (ii) above, the Managing Company will 
subsequently transfer the balances of the Cash Account back to the Financial Agent, 
provided that the non-subordinated and unsecured short-term debt of Barclays Bank 
PLC is assigned the aforementioned A-1, P-1 and F1 ratings and the stake held by 
Barclays Bank PLC in the Financial Agent is equal or higher than 51%. The 
substitution of the Financial Agent will in no event negatively affect the ratings of the 
Notes. Likewise, in the event that the credit rating of the non-subordinated and 
unsecured short-term debt of Barclays Bank PLC falls to A-1 (according to the rating 
scales for short-term risks of S&P), if the balance of the Cash Account exceeds 20% of 
the Unpaid Principal Balance of the Notes on a given Payment Date, the Managing 
Company will deposit the difference on the Excess Balance Account opened by the 
Managing Company in another credit entity whose short-term debt is assigned a 
minimum rating of A-1+ (in accordance the aforementioned rating scale), agreeing for 
the best obtainable return of such balance. Similarly, in the event that the non-
subordinated and unsecured short-term debt of Barclays Bank PLC attains again the 
A-1+ rating (in accordance with S&P short-term debt rating scale), the Managing 
Company will subsequently transfer to the Cash Account opened with the Financial 
Agent the then balance of the Excess Balance Account.  
(viii) 
It shall appoint the auditors of the Fund. 
 
 
86 


 
(ix) 
It shall manage the Fund with the objective of maintaining the net value of 
the Fund at zero at all times. 
(x) 
In accordance with the Prospectus and the Incorporation Deed, it shall 
adopt the appropriate resolutions with regard to the liquidation of the Fund, including 
the resolution for the early liquidation of the Fund. 
(xi) 
It shall perform its activity due diligently, as prescribed by Royal Decree 
926/1998, of May 14, representing the Fund and defending the interests of the 
holders of the Notes and of the Fund’s other ordinary creditors as if they were its own 
interests, stepping up the standards of diligence, reporting and defence of their 
interests and avoiding situations which might result in conflicts of interest, giving the 
interests of the holders of the Notes and all other ordinary creditors of the Fund 
priority over third-party and its own interests. In this regard, and without prejudice to 
the above, the Managing Company may be the managing company of other 
Securitisation Funds. The simultaneous management thereof shall not howsoever 
infringe its due diligence obligations as Managing Company of the Fund or of other 
Securitisation Funds. 
(xii) 
It shall have the necessary means, including suitable information systems, to 
discharge the Fund management functions prescribed by Royal Decree 926/1998, of 
May 14. 
(xiii) 
The Managing Company complies with the code of conduct applicable to it. 
The Managing Company has established a code of conduct pursuant to the provisions 
of Chapter II of Royal Decree 629/1993, of May 3, regarding the rules of conduct in 
securities markets and mandatory registrations. The said code of conduct has been 
amended in accordance with Law 44/2002 of November 22, on Measures for the 
Reform of the Financial System and has been communicated to the CNMV. 
(xiv) 
It shall check that the information provided by the Manager regarding 
amounts which are due, collected amounts, unpaid amounts, principal early 
repayments and recovery of unpaid amounts, in addition to other potential incomes, 
does conform with the amounts effectively deposited in the Cash Account of the Fund. 
(xv) 
It shall provide the holders of the Notes, the CNMV and the Rating Agencies 
with any informations and notifications whatsoever which may be required by the 
applicable Law and, in particular, with those herein contemplated, in the form 
provided in each case. 
(xvi) 
It shall notify the mortgage debtors of the change of Manager, in the event 
that Barclays Bank, S.A. is replaced as Manager of the Participated Mortgage Loans. 
Likewise, the Manager has undertaken to cooperate diligently in the transfer of the 
said documents and records and, in particular, to carry out whatever communications 
to the debtors that may be required under the Participated Mortgage Loans for the 
purposes of notifying the appointment of the new manager, the modifications in the 
 
 
87 


 
accounts for payments by direct debiting under the Participated Mortgage Loans and, 
generally, the alterations in the management procedure for collections which may be 
required for the avoidance of any damage to the Fund, all the above in accordance 
with the instructions given by the Managing Company. 
III.3.2. Remuneration of the Managing Company for performing its duties 
The Managing Company, in accordance with Law 19/1992, will incorporate, represent 
and manage the Fund. For these duties, the Fund will pay the Managing Company a 
Management Fee which includes an Initial Fee and a Periodic Fee. 
The Incorporation Deed will provide that the Managing Company will be entitled to an 
Initial Management Fee payable on the Disbursement Date in one lump sum 
amounting to 90,000 euros. 
The Incorporation Deed will also provide that the Managing Company will be entitled 
on each Payment Date to a Management Periodic Fee of an annual 0.02% of the sum 
of the amount of Mortgage Shares pending repayment on the previous Calculation 
Date, subject to a minimum amount of 30,050 euros and a maximum amount of 
150,000 euros per year. 
The calculation of the fee that will be paid on a given Payment Date, will be made by 
means of the following formula: 
C = B x 0.02% x d/365 
Being: 
C = Fee payable on a given Payment Date.   
B = Principal Balance of the amount of Mortgage Shares pending repayment on the 
previous Calculation Date.   
d = Number of days elapsed during the relevant accrual period (except for the first 
accrual period, where the days elapsed from the Incorporation Date until the first 
Payment Date will be considered). 
If during the life of the Fund, the Consumer Price Index published by the National 
Institute of Statistics corresponding to every calendar year rises, the annual minimum 
amount shall be adjusted cumulatively in the same proportion (the adjustment of the 
minimum amount being made according to the variation experienced by the 
Consumer Price Index of the previous year), starting from the year 2006 inclusive and 
effective from January 1 of every year. 
The fees referred to in the previous paragraphs are ranked first (1st) in the payment 
priority order established in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules set out in 
paragraph V.5.2. and are ranked first (1st) in the payment priority order in the event 
 
 
88 


 
of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph V.6.1. and the exceptional rules 
established in paragraph V.6.2. 
If, on a Payment Date, the Fund should not have enough liquidity to satisfy the 
Management Periodic Fee, the amount due will accrue interest equal to the addition of 
(i) the reference interest rate of the Notes (3 Month-EURIBOR calculated in 
accordance with paragraph II.10 of this Prospectus or the reference interest rate 
resulting from the interpolation provided for the first Interest Accrual Period) 
applicable in the relevant period and (ii) the final spread of Class D Notes payable on 
the following Payment Date, provided that the Fund has enough liquidity, in 
accordance with the payment priority order established in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and 
the exceptional rules set out in paragraph V.5.2. and the payment priority order in the 
event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph V.6.1. and the exceptional 
rules established in paragraph V.6.2. 
All payments to third parties in respect of ordinary expenses (such as annual audits of 
the Fund, publications and other) and extraordinary expenses related to the 
management of the Fund, will be satisfied by the Managing Company, in the name 
and on behalf of the Fund, represented by the Managing Company, whenever the 
Fund has enough liquidity for it, in accordance with the payment ranking established 
in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules set out in paragraph V.5.2. and the 
payment priority order in the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph 
V.6.1. and the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.6.2.

In accordance with Article 5.1 of Law 19/1992, the Fund constitutes a separate and 
closed estate, without a separate and independent legal status. As regards its assets, 
the Fund is composed of the Mortgage Shares and the Reserve Fund referred  to in 
paragraph V.3.4 and, as regards its liabilities, it is composed of the Notes and the 
Subordinated Loans (referred in paragraphs V.3.2 and V.3.3) in such a way that the 
net value of the Fund is zero. 
The description, characteristics and price of issue of the Mortgage Shares grouped in 
the Fund and of the Participated Mortgage Loans, are provided in Chapter IV of the 
Prospectus. The information regarding the Notes is provided in Chapter II.

III.4.3. Expenses incurred by the Fund 
 
Ordinary expenses are those which are to occur for certain during each fiscal year of 
the Fund and they are estimated for the purposes of the calculations made in the 
charts contained in this Prospectus at Euro 27,900 per year. This estimate considers 
the ordinary expenses referred to in paragraphs (b), (i) and (j) of the list of expenses 
which follows, that is, the fees of the Rating Agencies for the maintenance of the 
rating of all Classes of Notes, the expenses derived from the announcements and 
notifications related with the Fund and the Notes, and the expenses of audits and of 
legal advice, performed after the incorporation of the Fund. On the contrary, 
extraordinary expenses are those which are potentially to occur during each fiscal 
year of the Fund (as a result, their amount cannot be anticipated).  
Incorporation expenses 
The estimation of the Fund incorporation expenses is included in paragraph II.14. 
Periodic expenses and other expenses incurred during the life of the Fund 
The Managing Company shall satisfy, on account of the Fund, all the necessary 
expenses for its operation, according to the payment ranking established in paragraph 
V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules set out in paragraph V.5.2 and the payment 
priority order in the event of liquidation of the Fund contained in paragraph V.6.1. and 
the exceptional rules established in paragraph V.6.2.which correspond to each of 
them. Without limitation, the Managing Company will satisfy the following expenses: 
 
 
92 


 
(a) expenses of verifications, registrations and legally mandatory administrative 
authorisations that, as the case may be, should be obtained after the 
incorporation of the Fund; 
(b) fees of the Rating Agencies for the maintenance of the rating of all Classes of 
Notes; 
(c) expenses derived from the repayment of the Notes; 
(d) expenses regarding the maintenance of the book-entry records of the Notes and, 
if applicable, the maintenance of their listing in secondary markets or their 
representation by means of book entries; 
(e) expenses that may be derived from the sale of the Mortgage Shares and of the 
remaining assets of the Fund for its liquidation; 
(f) necessary expenses to initiate the enforcement of the Participated Mortgage 
Loans; 
(g) expenses derived from the management of the Fund and the management of the 
Participated Mortgage Loans. 
(h) fees and expenses, charged to the Fund, for the executed service agreements 
and  financial operations agreements; 
(i) 
expenses derived from the announcements and notifications related with the 
Fund and the Notes;   
(j) expenses of audits and of legal advice, performed after the incorporation of the 
Fund;   
(k) interest on the Notes; 
(l) 
interest on the Initial Expenses and Reserve Fund Subordinated Loans; 
(m) any amount payable by the Fund by virtue of the Interest Swap Agreement; and 
(n) in general, any other expenses supported by the Fund or by the Managing 
Company in the name and on behalf of the Fund. 
The Value Added Tax that the Fund may have supported will constitute 
deductible expenditure for the purposes of the Corporate Income Tax. 
III.5. 
Drawing-up, verification and approval of annual accounts and other 
accounting documentation of the Fund 
III.5.1. Obligations and foreseen terms for the drawing-up, verification and 
approval of the annual accounts and management report. 
 
 
93 


 
The annual accounts of the Fund will be annually verified and inspected by auditors.   
The Managing Company, on an annual basis, as soon as the annual accounts are 
available after their approval, which shall take place on April 30 of each year at the 
latest, shall file with the CNMV the annual accounts (balance sheet, profit and loss 
account and report), the managing report and the audit report of the Fund 
corresponding to the preceding fiscal year. The Managing Company shall also file 
them with the Commercial Registry, provided that it is legally required. 
The Managing Company shall designate an Auditor to carry out, during that period, 
the audit of the annual accounts of the Fund, reporting such appointment to the 
CNMV. Likewise, the Managing Company shall communicate the CNMV, in the form 
provided in paragraph III.5.3. b), of any change in connection with the appointment 
of the Auditor. 
III.5.2. Obligations and foreseen terms for the disclosure to the public and 
submission to the CNMV of the periodic information of the economic-
financial situation of the Fund  
The Managing Company, as manager and administrator of the Fund, undertakes to 
submit to the CNMV, as promptly as possible, the information indicated below, within 
a term of one month following to each Payment Date, except the information 
contained in paragraph e) which will be submitted annually, in relation to all Classes 
of Notes, the performance of the Mortgage Shares, anticipated repayments and the 
economic-financial situation of the Fund, without prejudice to serving the ordinary or 
extraordinary periodic notifications referred to in paragraph III.5.3 and to supplying all 
additional information which may be required.

1.

Accrued and paid interest.

Principal Balance. 
2. 
Accrued and collected interest.

3.

accordance with the payment priority order of paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the 
exceptional rules set out in paragraph V.5.2. 
d) With regard to the early repayment of the Participated Mortgage Loans 
The actual average rate of prepayment of the Participated Mortgage Loans 
corresponding to the analysed period, as well as the average life of the Notes 
assuming the hypothesis of maintenance of such average rates of prepayment. 
e) Annually, with regard to the Annual Accounts of the Fund 
The Balance Sheet, the Profit & Loss Account, the Report, the Management 
Report and the Audit Report, as soon as they are available after their approval, 
which shall take place on April 30 of each year at the latest. 
III.5.3. Obligations of communication of relevant facts 
The Managing Company undertakes, for the sake of accurate compliance with the 
conditions of the issue, to serve the notices which are detailed below. 
a) 
Regular ordinary notices 
1. 
Within the term comprised between the Interest Rate Fixing Date and the next 
two (2) Business Days following each Payment Date, the Managing Company will 
inform the Noteholders of the Nominal Interest Rates which apply for each Class 
of Notes for the next Interest Accrual Period following the criteria described in 
paragraph II.10.1. 
2. 
At least one (1) calendar day in advance of each Payment Date, the interest rates 
which apply for the Notes of each Class, together with their repayment, if 
applicable, in addition to: 
i) 
the actual rates of early repayment of the Participated Mortgages Loans on 
the Calculation Date prior to the Payment Date; 
ii) 
the average remaining term of the Notes estimated on the assumption that 
such actual rate of early repayment remains constant in accordance with 
paragraph II.11.3.3; 
 
 
95 


 
iii) the Unpaid Principal Balances of the Notes of each Class after repayment to 
be settled on each Payment Date, and the percentages represented by such 
Unpaid Principal Balances over the initial nominal amount of the Notes; 
iv) if applicable, the Noteholders will be informed of the amounts of interest and 
principal due for repayment which have accrued and remain unpaid due to a 
lack of Available Funds, in accordance with the payment priority order 
established in paragraph V.5.1.B)2 and the exceptional rules set out in 
paragraph V.5.2. 
The above notices will also be given to Sociedad de Gestión de los Sistemas de 
Registro, Compensación y Liquidación de Valores, S.A., the governing authority of 
AIAF and the Financial Agent at least one (1) Business Day in advance to each 
Payment Date following the conditions established in paragraph c) below. 
3. 
Within seven (7) Business Days following each Payment Date, the Managing 
Company will issue a certification signed by a duly empowered person, which will 
provide evidence of: the Unpaid Principal Balances of the Notes, the Principal 
Deficiency, if any, and if applicable, the amount of interest accrued and unpaid to 
the Noteholders in accordance with paragraph II.10.3 
Such certification will be submitted to the CNMV, to the entity in charge of the 
accounting records and to the governing authority of the AIAF, to make it 
available to the public together with the Incorporation Deed. 
b) Extraordinary notices 
 
t
1.

Business Day, being suitable for such  publication. 
As an exception, the Nominal Interest Rates of all Classes of Notes determined 
for the first Interest Accrual Period (which will run between the Disbursement 
Date and the first Payment Date) and the final spreads applicable to each Class

Others 
The Managing Company, in the name and on behalf of the Fund, will inform the 
Noteholders of any relevant fact which might have occurred in connection with

and the Rating Agencies as soon as it is available. 
c) 
Procedure
